69891_12_ITEM1_P0_S0	National Beverage Corp. is an acknowledged leader in the development, manufacturing, marketing and sale of a diverse portfolio of flavored beverage products.
69891_12_ITEM1_P0_S1	Our primary focus is the United States, but our products are also distributed in Canada, Mexico, the Caribbean, Latin America, the Pacific Rim, Asia, Europe and the Middle East.
69891_12_ITEM1_P1_S0	A holding company for various operating subsidiaries, National Beverage Corp. was incorporated in Delaware in 1985 and began trading as a public company on the NASDAQ Stock Market in 1991.
69891_12_ITEM1_P1_S1	In this report, the terms we, us, our, Company and National Beverage mean National Beverage Corp. and its subsidiaries unless indicated otherwise.
69891_12_ITEM1_P2_S0	Our brands include soft drinks, energy drinks and shots, juices, teas, still and sparkling waters and nutritionally enhanced beverages, and span both carbonated and non-carbonated offerings.
69891_12_ITEM1_P2_S1	In addition, we produce soft drinks for certain retailers ( Allied Brands ) who also promote certain of our brands ( Strategic Alliances ).
69891_12_ITEM1_P2_S2	We employ a philosophy that demands vertical integration wherever possible and our vertically integrated manufacturing model unites the procurement of raw materials, production of concentrates and manufacturing of finished products in our twelve manufacturing facilities.
69891_12_ITEM1_P2_S3	To service a diverse customer base that includes numerous national retailers as well as hundreds of smaller up and down the street accounts, we have developed a hybrid distribution system which promotes and utilizes customers warehouse distribution facilities and our own direct-store delivery fleet plus the direct-store delivery systems of independent distributors and wholesalers.
69891_12_ITEM1_P3_S0	We believe that the combination of our business strategies and philosophies is key to giving us a greater competitive advantage and differentiating us from our competitors.
69891_12_ITEM1_P4_S0	Fantasy of Flavors - Throughout our product lines, we emphasize distinctly flavored beverages.
69891_12_ITEM1_P5_S0	Although cola drinks account for approximately 50% of the soft drink industry s domestic grocery channel volume, colas account for less than 20% of our total volume.
69891_12_ITEM1_P5_S1	In the higher margin convenience store channel, flavors now represent 56% of soft drink sales and are growing significantly faster than colas.
69891_12_ITEM1_P5_S2	Our flavor development spans more than 100 years and originated with our flagship brands, Shasta and Faygo, each of which offer over 50 flavor varieties.
69891_12_ITEM1_P6_S0	Regional Share Dynamics This is our term for the philosophy we employ for the development and support of our brands that have significant regional presence.
69891_12_ITEM1_P6_S1	Because we tailor our marketing and promotion programs by locale, we believe many of our brands enjoy a regional identification that fosters long-term consumer loyalty and make them less vulnerable to competitive substitution.
69891_12_ITEM1_P6_S2	In addition, home-town products often generate more aggressive retailer sponsored promotional activities and receive media exposure through community activities rather than costly national advertising.
69891_12_ITEM1_P7_S0	We believe that consumers demand value as the purchase default option in volatile economic times, and we are intent on producing and developing products of the highest quality that appeal to the value expectations of the family consumer.
69891_12_ITEM1_P7_S1	We believe we can leverage our cost-effective manufacturing and distribution systems, and our efficient regionally focused marketing programs, to profitably deliver products to the consumer at a lower price-point than our national competitors.
69891_12_ITEM1_P8_S0	Creative Agility - In a beverage industry that is dominated by the cola giants , we pride ourselves on our ability to respond faster and more creatively to consumer trends than many of our competitors which are burdened by distribution complexity and legacy costs.
69891_12_ITEM1_P8_S1	We strive to build long-term brand value by developing creative marketing programs, propriety flavors and distinctive packaging.
69891_12_ITEM1_P8_S2	During the past year we have introduced 54 new flavors or package sizes, and have won various package design awards.
69891_12_ITEM1_P8_S3	During recent years, we have focused on developing innovative beverages tailored toward healthy lifestyles and introducing products and package sizes designed to expand distribution in the higher-margin convenience store channel.
69891_12_ITEM1_P8_S4	We believe that the most dynamic validation of our strategy is our competitors efforts to replicate our creative business model.
69891_12_ITEM1_P9_S0	Established more than 120 years ago and distributed nationally, Shasta is recognized to be a bottling industry pioneer and innovator.
69891_12_ITEM1_P9_S1	As our largest volume brand, Shasta features multiple flavors, including products targeted to the growing Hispanic and other ethnic markets, and continues to earn consumer loyalty by delivering value, convenience and unique tastes such as California Dreamin , Very Cherry Twist and Fiesta Punch.
69891_12_ITEM1_P10_S0	More than one hundred years old, Faygo products are primarily distributed east of the Mississippi River and include numerous unique flavors including RedPop, Moon Mist and Rock n Rye .
69891_12_ITEM1_P10_S1	We also produce and market Ritz soft drinks and seltzers, primarily in the southeast U.S., and distribute Big Shot in New Orleans and the surrounding areas.
69891_12_ITEM1_P11_S0	Rip It, our energy fuel which is available nationally in 17 flavors including five sugar free varieties, is the number one energy drink in the dollar-store channel.
69891_12_ITEM1_P11_S1	Building on the success of Rip It, we recently introduced two-ounce Rip It Shots in five flavors, including a new G-Force Extra Strength Formula.
69891_12_ITEM1_P11_S2	For consumers seeking vitamin-enhanced hydration, we offer Mega Sport in six reinvigorating flavors.
69891_12_ITEM1_P12_S0	Everfresh and its sister brands, Home Juice and Mr. Pure, 100% fresh juice and juice-added products, are available in over 30 flavors including Blueberry Pomegranate, Kiwi Strawberry and Pineapple Mango.
69891_12_ITEM1_P12_S1	Originating in the Midwest over 50 years ago, these brands feature unique glass packaging targeted primarily for single-serve consumption.
69891_12_ITEM1_P13_S0	As the most agile regional juice company, we have been successfully expanding to new geographic areas through both independent and Company-owned distribution facilities.
69891_12_ITEM1_P14_S0	With all natural ingredients, LaCroix has been outpacing the growing sparkling water segment that is fast becoming the alternative to traditional carbonated soft drinks.
69891_12_ITEM1_P14_S1	Containing no calories, sodium or caffeine, LaCroix has benefited from the support of major national chains and is the number one selling canned sparkling water in the U.S. as well as the number one domestically produced sparkling water.
69891_12_ITEM1_P14_S2	With new packages being designed for non-traditional distribution channels, we believe LaCroix is uniquely positioned to continue expanding its national footprint.
69891_12_ITEM1_P14_S3	Other products we offer the health-conscious consumer include Clear Fruit, a clean crisp all natural non-carbonated beverage; Crystal Bay, a zero-calorie combination of sparkling water and lively fruit flavors; sant , a 50-calorie vitamin enhanced nutraceutical beverage; and Mt. Shasta, a natural spring water.
69891_12_ITEM1_P15_S0	Our other non-carbonated products include the Ohana line of fruit drinks, lemonades and teas, and the Sundance line, which features brewed tea combined with great fruit flavors and reduced calories.
69891_12_ITEM1_P16_S0	We refer to our portfolio of brands other than soft drinks as our Power+ Brands .
69891_12_ITEM1_P17_S0	Our twelve manufacturing facilities are strategically located near major metropolitan markets across the continental United States.
69891_12_ITEM1_P17_S1	The locations of our plants enable us to efficiently manufacture and distribute beverages to substantially all geographic markets in the United States, including 22 of the top 25 metropolitan statistical areas.
69891_12_ITEM1_P17_S2	Each manufacturing facility is generally equipped to produce both canned and bottled beverage products in a variety of package sizes.
69891_12_ITEM1_P17_S3	We utilize numerous package types and sizes, including cans ranging from eight to sixteen ounces and bottles ranging from seven ounces to three liters.
69891_12_ITEM1_P18_S0	We believe that the innovative and controlled vertical integration of our bottling facilities provides an advantage over certain of our competitors that rely upon independent third party bottlers to manufacture and market their products.
69891_12_ITEM1_P18_S1	Since we control the national production, distribution and marketing of our brands, we believe we can more effectively manage product quality and customer service and respond quickly to changing market conditions.
69891_12_ITEM1_P19_S0	We produce a substantial portion of the flavor concentrates used in our branded products.
69891_12_ITEM1_P19_S1	By controlling our own formulas throughout our bottling network, we can manufacture our products in accordance with uniform quality standards while tailoring flavors to regional taste preferences.
69891_12_ITEM1_P19_S2	We believe that the combination of a Company-owned bottling network, together with uniform standards for packaging, formulations and customer service, provides us with a strategic advantage in servicing national retailers and mass-merchandisers.
69891_12_ITEM1_P19_S3	We also maintain research and development laboratories at multiple locations.
69891_12_ITEM1_P19_S4	These laboratories continually test products for compliance with our strict quality control standards as well as conduct research for new products and flavors.
69891_12_ITEM1_P20_S0	We utilize a hybrid distribution system to deliver our products through three primary distribution channels: take-home, convenience and food-service.
69891_12_ITEM1_P21_S0	The take-home distribution channel consists of national and regional grocery stores, warehouse clubs, mass-merchandisers, wholesalers and dollar stores.
69891_12_ITEM1_P21_S1	We distribute our products to this channel through the warehouse distribution system and the direct-store delivery system.
69891_12_ITEM1_P22_S0	Under the warehouse distribution system, products are shipped from our manufacturing facilities to the retailer s centralized distribution centers and then distributed by the retailer to each of its outlet locations with other goods.
69891_12_ITEM1_P22_S1	Products sold through the direct-store delivery system are distributed directly to the customer s retail outlets by our direct-store delivery fleet and by independent distributors.
69891_12_ITEM1_P23_S0	We distribute our products to the convenience channel through our own direct-store delivery fleet and those of independent distributors.
69891_12_ITEM1_P24_S0	The convenience channel consists of convenience stores, gas stations and other smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts.
69891_12_ITEM1_P24_S1	Because of the higher retail prices and margins that typically prevail, we have undertaken several measures to expand convenience channel distribution.
69891_12_ITEM1_P24_S2	These include development of products, packaging and graphics specifically targeted to this market.
69891_12_ITEM1_P25_S0	Our food-service division distributes products to independent, specialized distributors who sell to hospitals, schools, military bases, airlines, hotels and food-service wholesalers.
69891_12_ITEM1_P25_S1	Also, our Company-owned direct-store delivery fleet distributes products to certain schools and other food service customers.
69891_12_ITEM1_P26_S0	Our take-home, convenience and food-service operations use vending machines and glass-door coolers as marketing and promotional tools for our brands.
69891_12_ITEM1_P26_S1	We provide vending machines and coolers on a placement or purchase basis to our customers.
69891_12_ITEM1_P26_S2	We believe vending and cooler equipment increases beverage sales, enhances brand awareness and develops brand loyalty.
69891_12_ITEM1_P27_S0	In addition to foreign based customers, we distribute our brands outside of the United States through exporters and foreign locations of U.S. based companies.
69891_12_ITEM1_P28_S0	We sell and market our products through an internal sales force as well as select broker networks.
69891_12_ITEM1_P28_S1	Our sales force is organized to serve a specific market, focusing on one or more geographic territories, distribution channels or product lines.
69891_12_ITEM1_P28_S2	We believe this focus allows our sales group to provide high level, responsive service and support to our customers and markets.
69891_12_ITEM1_P29_S0	Our sales and marketing programs emphasize maintaining and enhancing consumer brand recognition and loyalty and typically utilize a combination of regional advertising, special event marketing, endorsements and sponsorships, along with consumer coupon distribution.
69891_12_ITEM1_P29_S1	We retain advertising agencies to assist with media advertising programs for our brands.
69891_12_ITEM1_P29_S2	Additionally, we offer numerous promotional programs to retail customers, including cooperative advertising support, in-store advertising materials and other incentives.
69891_12_ITEM1_P29_S3	These elements allow us to tailor marketing and advertising programs to meet local and regional economic conditions and demographics.
69891_12_ITEM1_P29_S4	Additionally, we sponsor special holiday promotions which feature St. Nick s soft drink and special holiday flavors and packaging.
69891_12_ITEM1_P30_S0	Our centralized procurement group maintains relationships with numerous suppliers of raw materials and packaging goods.
69891_12_ITEM1_P30_S1	By consolidating the purchasing function for our manufacturing facilities, we believe we are able to procure more competitive arrangements with our suppliers, thereby allowing us to compete as a low-cost producer of beverages.
69891_12_ITEM1_P31_S0	The products we produce and sell are made from various materials including sweeteners, juice concentrates, carbon dioxide, water, glass and plastic bottles, aluminum cans and ends, paper, cartons and closures.
69891_12_ITEM1_P31_S1	Most of our low-calorie soft drink products use sucralose, aspartame, stevia or Acesulfame-K. We manufacture a substantial portion of our flavor concentrates and purchase remaining raw materials from multiple suppliers.
69891_12_ITEM1_P32_S0	Substantially all of the materials and ingredients we purchase are presently available from several suppliers, although strikes, weather conditions, utility shortages, governmental control or regulations, national emergencies, price or supply fluctuations or other events outside our control could adversely affect the supply of specific materials.
69891_12_ITEM1_P32_S1	A significant portion of our raw material purchases, including aluminum cans, plastic bottles, high fructose corn syrup, corregated packaging and juice concentrates, are derived from commodities.
69891_12_ITEM1_P32_S2	Therefore, pricing and availability tend to fluctuate based upon worldwide market conditions.
69891_12_ITEM1_P32_S3	Our ability to recover increased costs through higher pricing may be limited by the competitive environment in which we operate.
69891_12_ITEM1_P32_S4	In certain cases, we may elect to enter into multi-year agreements for the supply of these materials with one or more suppliers, the terms of which may include variable or fixed pricing, minimum purchase quantities and/or the requirement to purchase all supplies for specified locations.
69891_12_ITEM1_P32_S5	Additionally, we use derivative financial instruments to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in certain raw material costs.
69891_12_ITEM1_P33_S0	The majority of our sales are seasonal with the highest volume typically realized during the summer months.
69891_12_ITEM1_P33_S1	We have sufficient production capacity to meet seasonal increases without maintaining significant quantities of inventory in anticipation of periods of peak demand.
69891_12_ITEM1_P33_S2	Additionally, our sales are affected by weather conditions.
69891_12_ITEM1_P34_S0	The beverage industry is highly competitive and our competitive position varies in each of our market areas.
69891_12_ITEM1_P34_S1	Our products compete with many varieties of liquid refreshment, including soft drinks, water products, juices, fruit drinks, powdered drinks, coffees, teas, energy drinks, sports drinks, dairy-based drinks, functional beverages and various other nonalcoholic beverages.
69891_12_ITEM1_P34_S2	We compete with bottlers and distributors of national, regional and private label products.
69891_12_ITEM1_P34_S3	Several competitors, including the two that dominate the soft drink industry, PepsiCo, Inc. and The Coca-Cola Company, have greater financial resources than we have and aggressive promotion of their products can adversely affect sales of our brands.
69891_12_ITEM1_P34_S4	Principal methods of competition in the beverage industry are price and promotional activity, advertising and marketing programs, point-of-sale merchandising, retail space management, customer service, product differentiation, packaging innovations and distribution methods.
69891_12_ITEM1_P34_S5	We believe our Company differentiates itself through a diversified product portfolio, strong regional brand recognition, innovative flavor variety, attractive packaging, efficient distribution methods, specialized advertising and, for some product lines, value pricing.
69891_12_ITEM1_P35_S0	We own numerous trademarks for our brands that are significant to our business.
69891_12_ITEM1_P35_S1	We intend to continue to maintain all registrations of our significant trademarks and use the trademarks in the operation of our businesses.
69891_12_ITEM1_P36_S0	The production, distribution and sale of our products in the United States are subject to the Federal Food, Drug and Cosmetic Act; the Dietary Supplement Health and Education Act of 1994; the Occupational Safety and Health Act; the Lanham Act; various environmental statutes; and various other federal, state and local statutes regulating the production, transportation, sale, safety, advertising, labeling and ingredients of such products.
69891_12_ITEM1_P36_S1	Our management believes that we are in compliance, in all material respects, with such existing legislation.
69891_12_ITEM1_P37_S0	Certain states and localities prohibit the sale of certain beverages unless a deposit or tax is charged for containers.
69891_12_ITEM1_P37_S1	These requirements vary by each jurisdiction.
69891_12_ITEM1_P37_S2	Similar legislation has been proposed in certain other states and localities, as well as by Congress.
69891_12_ITEM1_P37_S3	We are unable to predict whether such legislation will be enacted or what impact its enactment would have on our business, financial condition or results of operations.
69891_12_ITEM1_P38_S0	All of our facilities in the United States are subject to federal, state and local environmental laws and regulations.
69891_12_ITEM1_P38_S1	Compliance with these provisions has not had any material adverse effect on our financial or competitive position.
69891_12_ITEM1_P38_S2	We believe that our current practices and procedures for the control and disposition of toxic or hazardous substances comply in all material respects with applicable law.
69891_12_ITEM1_P38_S3	Compliance with or violation of any current or future regulations could require material expenditures or have a material adverse effect on our financial results.
69891_12_ITEM1_P39_S0	As of April 28, 2012, we employed approximately 1,200 people, of which approximately 300 are covered by collective bargaining agreements.
69891_12_ITEM1_P40_S0	We believe that relations with employees are generally good.
69891_12_ITEM1_P41_S0	Our Annual Reports on Form 10-K, Quarterly Reports on Form 10-Q, Current Reports on Form 8-K, proxy statements and amendments to those reports are available free of charge on our website at www.nationalbeverage.com as soon as reasonably practicable after such reports are electronically filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission.
69891_12_ITEM1_P41_S1	In addition, our Code of Ethics is available on our website.
69891_12_ITEM1_P41_S2	The information on the Company s website is not part of this Annual Report on Form 10-K or any other report that we file with, or furnish to, the Securities and Exchange Commission.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P0_S0	In addition to other information in this Form 10-K, the following risk factors should be considered carefully in evaluating the Company s business.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P0_S1	Our business, financial condition and results of operations could be materially and adversely affected by any of these risks.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P0_S2	Additional risks and uncertainties, including risks and uncertainties not presently known to the Company, or that the Company currently deems immaterial, may also impair our business and results of operations.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P1_S0	Changes in consumer preferences and taste.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P1_S1	There has been an increasing focus on health and wellness by beverage consumers, which may reduce demand for caloric carbonated soft drinks and increase the consumption of products perceived to deliver health, wellness and/or functionality.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P2_S0	If we do not adequately anticipate and react to changing demographics, consumer trends, health concerns and product preferences, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P3_S0	The beverage industry is extremely competitive.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P3_S1	Our products compete with a broad range of beverage products, most of which are manufactured and distributed by companies with substantially greater financial, marketing and distribution resources.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P3_S2	In order to generate future revenues and profits, we must continue to sell products that appeal to our customers and consumers.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P3_S3	Discounting and other actions by our competitors may make it more difficult to sustain revenues and profits.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P4_S0	Our retail customer base has been consolidating over the last several years resulting in fewer customers with increased purchasing power.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P4_S1	This increased purchasing power can limit our ability to increase pricing for our products with certain of our customers.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P4_S2	Our inability to meet the demands of our larger customers could lead to a loss of business and adversely affect our financial results.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P5_S0	The production of our products is dependent on certain raw materials, including aluminum, resin, corn, linerboard and fruit juice.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P5_S1	In addition, the production and distribution of our products is dependent on energy sources, including natural gas, fuel and electricity.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P5_S2	These items are subject to price volatility caused by numerous factors.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P5_S3	Commodity price increases ultimately result in a corresponding increase in the cost of raw materials and energy.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P5_S4	We may be limited in our ability to pass these increases on to our customers or may incur a loss in sales volume to the extent price increases are taken.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P5_S5	In addition, strikes, weather conditions, governmental controls, national emergencies, natural disasters, supply shortages or other events could affect our continued supply of raw materials and energy.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P5_S6	If raw materials or energy costs increase, or the availability is limited, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P6_S0	Our business and properties are subject to various federal, state and local laws and regulations, including those governing the production, packaging, quality, labeling and distribution of beverage products.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P6_S1	In addition, various governmental agencies have considered imposing taxes on soft drinks and other sugar-sweetened beverages, including those sweetened with high fructose corn syrup.
69891_12_ITEM1A_P6_S2	New laws or regulations or changes in existing laws or regulations could negatively affect our financial results through lower sales or higher operating costs.
69891_12_ITEM2_P0_S0	Our principal properties include twelve manufacturing facilities located in ten states, which aggregate approximately two million square feet.
69891_12_ITEM2_P0_S1	We own ten manufacturing facilities in the following states: California (2), Georgia, Kansas, Michigan (2), Ohio, Texas, Utah and Washington.
69891_12_ITEM2_P0_S2	Two manufacturing facilities, located in Maryland and Florida, are leased subject to agreements that expire through 2020.
69891_12_ITEM2_P0_S3	We believe our facilities are generally in good condition and sufficient to meet our present needs.
69891_12_ITEM2_P1_S0	The production of beverages is capital intensive but is not characterized by rapid technological change.
69891_12_ITEM2_P1_S1	The technological advances that have occurred have generally been of an incremental cost-saving nature, such as the industry s conversion to lighter weight containers or improved blending processes that enhance ingredient yields.
69891_12_ITEM2_P1_S2	We are not aware of any anticipated industry-wide changes in technology that would adversely impact our current physical production capacity or cost of production.
69891_12_ITEM2_P2_S0	We own and lease trucks, vans and automobiles used in the sale, delivery and distribution of our products.
69891_12_ITEM2_P2_S1	In addition, we lease office and warehouse space, transportation equipment, office equipment, information systems equipment and certain manufacturing equipment.
69891_12_ITEM3_P0_S0	From time to time, we are a party to various litigation matters arising in the ordinary course of business.
69891_12_ITEM3_P0_S1	We do not expect the ultimate disposition of such matters to have a material adverse effect on our consolidated financial position or results of operations.

69891_12_ITEM7_P0_S0	National Beverage Corp. is a holding company for various subsidiaries that develop, manufacture, market and sell a diverse portfolio of beverage products.
69891_12_ITEM7_P0_S1	In this report, the terms we, us, our, Company and National Beverage mean National Beverage Corp. and its subsidiaries unless indicated otherwise.
69891_12_ITEM7_P1_S0	Our brands include soft drinks, energy drinks and shots, juices, teas, still and sparkling waters and nutritionally enhanced beverages, and span both carbonated and non-carbonated offerings.
69891_12_ITEM7_P1_S1	In addition, we produce soft drinks for certain retailers ( Allied Brands ) who also promote certain of our brands ( Strategic Alliances ).
69891_12_ITEM7_P1_S2	We employee a philosophy that demands vertical integration wherever possible and our vertically integrated manufacturing model unites the procurement of raw materials, production of concentrates and manufacturing of finished products in our twelve manufacturing facilities.
69891_12_ITEM7_P1_S3	To service a diverse customer base that includes numerous national retailers as well as hundreds of smaller up and down the street accounts, we have developed a hybrid distribution system which promotes and utilizes customers warehouse distribution facilities and our own direct-store delivery fleet plus the direct-store delivery systems of independent distributors.
69891_12_ITEM7_P2_S0	We consider ourselves to be a leader in the development and sale of flavored beverage products.
69891_12_ITEM7_P2_S1	Our soft drink flavor development spans over 100 years originating with our flagship brands, Shasta and Faygo , and includes our Ritz and Big Shot brands.
69891_12_ITEM7_P2_S2	For the health-conscious consumer, we offer a diverse line of flavored beverage products, including Everfresh , Home Juice and Mr. Pure 100% juice and juice-based products; LaCroix , Crystal Bay and Clear Fruit flavored, sparkling and spring water products; and sant nutritionally-enhanced beverage.
69891_12_ITEM7_P2_S3	In addition, we produce and market Rip It energy drinks and shots, Ohana fruit-flavored non-carbonated drinks, Sundance teas and lemonades and St. Nick s holiday soft drinks.
69891_12_ITEM7_P2_S4	We refer to our portfolio of brands other than soft drinks as our Power+ Brands .
69891_12_ITEM7_P3_S0	Our strategy emphasizes the growth of our products by (i) offering a beverage portfolio of proprietary flavors with distinctive packaging and broad demographic appeal, (ii) supporting the franchise value of regional brands, (iii) appealing to the quality-value expectations of the family consumer and (iv) responding to demographic trends by developing innovative products tailored toward healthy lifestyles or designed to expand distribution in higher-margin channels.
69891_12_ITEM7_P4_S0	The majority of our sales are seasonal with the highest volume typically realized during the summer months.
69891_12_ITEM7_P4_S1	As a result, our operating results from one fiscal quarter to the next may not be comparable.
69891_12_ITEM7_P4_S2	Additionally, our operating results are affected by numerous factors, including fluctuations in the costs of raw materials, changes in consumer preference for beverage products, competitive pricing in the marketplace and weather conditions.
69891_12_ITEM7_P5_S0	Net sales for the fiscal year ended April 28, 2012 ( Fiscal 2012 ) increased 4.8% to $628.9 million as compared to $600.2 million for the fiscal year ended April 30, 2011 ( Fiscal 2011 ).
69891_12_ITEM7_P5_S1	The sales improvement is due to case volume growth of 9.9% for our Power+ Brands and 1.4% for carbonated soft drinks.
69891_12_ITEM7_P5_S2	In addition, our unit pricing increased 1.3% due to price increases implemented to offset higher raw material costs.
69891_12_ITEM7_P6_S0	Net sales for Fiscal 2011 increased 1.1% to $600.2 million as compared to $593.5 million for the fiscal year ended May 1, 2010 ( Fiscal 2010 ).
69891_12_ITEM7_P6_S1	The sales improvement is due to case volume growth of 13.2% for our Power+ Brands, and a 1.2% increase in unit pricing resulting from favorable product mix changes.
69891_12_ITEM7_P6_S2	This sales improvement was partially offset by a 2.1% volume decline for branded carbonated soft drinks due to weak demand in certain regional markets.
69891_12_ITEM7_P7_S0	Gross profit approximated 33.9% of net sales for Fiscal 2012, which represents a 2.5% margin decline compared to Fiscal 2011.
69891_12_ITEM7_P8_S0	During Fiscal 2011 we benefited from sales of certain high margin products to overseas locations.
69891_12_ITEM7_P8_S1	These sales were impacted during Fiscal 2012 and, accordingly, gross margins returned to more normalized levels.
69891_12_ITEM7_P8_S2	The gross margin decline is also due to higher raw material costs and other changes in product mix.
69891_12_ITEM7_P8_S3	Cost of sales increased 5.3% on a per case basis.
69891_12_ITEM7_P9_S0	Gross profit approximated 36.4% of net sales for Fiscal 2011, which represents a 3.2% margin improvement over Fiscal 2010.
69891_12_ITEM7_P9_S1	This gross margin improvement is primarily due to favorable changes in brand and package mix.
69891_12_ITEM7_P9_S2	Cost of sales decreased 3.7% on a per case basis.
69891_12_ITEM7_P10_S0	Shipping and handling costs are included in selling, general and administrative expenses, the classification of which is consistent with many beverage companies.
69891_12_ITEM7_P10_S1	However, our gross margin may not be comparable to companies that include shipping and handling costs in cost of sales.
69891_12_ITEM7_P10_S2	See Note 1 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements.

69891_12_ITEM7_P11_S1	The decline in expenses is due to a decrease in marketing and administrative expenses.
69891_12_ITEM7_P12_S0	Selling, general and administrative expenses were $155.9 million or 26.0% of net sales for Fiscal 2011 compared to $145.2 million or 24.5% of net sales for Fiscal 2010.
69891_12_ITEM7_P12_S1	The increase in expenses was primarily due to additional investment in expanded distribution, including expanded marketing and selling programs.
69891_12_ITEM7_P12_S2	Marketing costs reflect increased cooperative advertising programs with customers and increased brand support expenditures.

69891_12_ITEM7_P33_S0	We sell products to a variety of customers and extend credit based on an evaluation of each customer s financial condition, generally without requiring collateral.

69891_12_ITEM7_P35_S0	All long-lived assets, excluding goodwill and intangible assets not subject to amortization, are evaluated for impairment on the basis of undiscounted cash flows whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable.
69891_12_ITEM7_P35_S1	An impaired asset is written down to its estimated fair market value based on the best information available.
69891_12_ITEM7_P36_S0	Estimated fair market value is generally measured by discounting future cash flows.
69891_12_ITEM7_P37_S0	Goodwill and intangible assets not subject to amortization are evaluated for impairment annually or sooner if we believe such assets may be impaired.
69891_12_ITEM7_P37_S1	An impairment loss is recognized if the carrying amount or, for goodwill, the carrying amount of its reporting unit, is greater than its fair value.
69891_12_ITEM7_P38_S0	Our effective income tax rate is based on estimates of taxes which will ultimately be payable.

69891_12_ITEM7_P39_S1	Valuation allowances are established to reduce the carrying amounts of deferred tax assets when it is deemed, more likely than not, that the benefit of deferred tax assets will not be realized.

69891_12_ITEM7_P41_S0	We offer various sales incentive arrangements to our customers that require customer performance or achievement of certain sales volume targets.
69891_12_ITEM7_P41_S1	In those circumstances when the incentive is paid in advance, we amortize the amount paid over the period of benefit or contractual sales volume.
69891_12_ITEM7_P41_S2	When the incentive is paid in arrears, we accrue the expected amount to be paid over the period of benefit or expected sales volume.
69891_12_ITEM7_P41_S3	The recognition of these incentives involves the use of judgment related to performance and sales volume estimates that are made based on historical experience and other factors.
69891_12_ITEM7_P41_S4	Sales incentives are accounted for as a reduction of sales and actual amounts ultimately realized may vary from accrued amounts.

69891_12_ITEM8_P11_S1	An impairment loss is recognized if the carrying amount or, for goodwill, the carrying amount of its reporting unit, is greater than its fair value.
69891_12_ITEM8_P12_S0	Our effective income tax rate is based on estimates of taxes which will ultimately be payable.
69891_12_ITEM8_P13_S0	Deferred taxes are recorded to give recognition to temporary differences between the tax bases of assets or liabilities and their reported amounts in the financial statements.
69891_12_ITEM8_P13_S1	Valuation allowances are established to reduce the carrying amounts of deferred tax assets when it is deemed, more likely than not, that the benefit of deferred tax assets will not be realized.
69891_12_ITEM8_P14_S0	We maintain self-insured and deductible programs for certain liability, medical and workers compensation exposures.
69891_12_ITEM8_P14_S1	Accordingly, we accrue for known claims and estimated incurred but not reported claims not otherwise covered by insurance, based on actuarial assumptions and historical claims experience.
69891_12_ITEM8_P15_S0	Intangible assets as of April 28, 2012 and April 30, 2011 consisted of non-amortizable trademarks.
69891_12_ITEM8_P16_S0	Inventories are stated at the lower of first-in, first-out cost or market.
69891_12_ITEM8_P16_S1	Inventories at April 28, 2012 were comprised of finished goods of $24.4 million and raw materials of $16.5 million.
69891_12_ITEM8_P16_S2	Inventories at April 30, 2011 were comprised of finished goods of $20.2 million and raw materials of $13.1 million.
69891_12_ITEM8_P17_S0	We are involved in a variety of marketing programs, including cooperative advertising programs with customers, to advertise and promote our products to consumers.
69891_12_ITEM8_P17_S1	Marketing costs are expensed when incurred, except for prepaid advertising and production costs which are expensed when the advertising takes place.
69891_12_ITEM8_P17_S2	Marketing costs, which are included in selling, general and administrative expenses, totaled $45.8 million in Fiscal 2012, $52.9 million in Fiscal 2011 and $44.7 million in Fiscal 2010.
69891_12_ITEM8_P18_S0	Basic net income per share is computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during the period.
69891_12_ITEM8_P18_S1	Diluted net income per share is calculated in a similar manner, but includes the dilutive effect of stock options, which amounted to 181,000 shares in Fiscal 2012, 185,000 shares in Fiscal 2011 and 229,000 shares in Fiscal 2010.
69891_12_ITEM8_P18_S2	Options to purchase 291,000 shares in Fiscal 2011 and 18,000 shares in Fiscal 2010 were not included in the calculation of diluted net income per share because these options were anti-dilutive.
69891_12_ITEM8_P19_S0	Property, plant and equipment are recorded at cost.
69891_12_ITEM8_P19_S1	Additions, replacements and betterments are capitalized, while maintenance and repairs that do not extend the useful life of an asset are expensed as incurred.
69891_12_ITEM8_P19_S2	Depreciation is recorded using the straight-line method over estimated useful lives of 7 to 30 years for buildings and improvements, and 3 to 15 years for machinery and equipment.
69891_12_ITEM8_P19_S3	Leasehold improvements are amortized using the straight-line method over the shorter of the remaining lease term or the estimated useful life of the improvement.
69891_12_ITEM8_P20_S0	When assets are retired or otherwise disposed, the cost and accumulated depreciation are removed from the respective accounts and any related gain or loss is recognized.
69891_12_ITEM8_P21_S0	Revenue from product sales is recognized when title and risk of loss pass to the customer, which generally occurs upon delivery.
69891_12_ITEM8_P21_S1	Our policy is not to allow the return of products once they have been accepted by the customer.
69891_12_ITEM8_P21_S2	However, on occasion, we have accepted returns or issued credit to customers, primarily for damaged goods.
69891_12_ITEM8_P21_S3	The amounts have been immaterial and, accordingly, we do not provide a specific valuation allowance for sales returns.
69891_12_ITEM8_P22_S0	We offer various sales incentive arrangements to our customers that require customer performance or achievement of certain sales volume targets.
69891_12_ITEM8_P22_S1	In those circumstances when the incentive is paid in advance, we amortize the amount paid over the period of benefit or contractual sales volume.
69891_12_ITEM8_P22_S2	When the incentive is paid in arrears, we accrue the expected amount to be paid over the period of benefit or expected sales volume.
69891_12_ITEM8_P22_S3	The recognition of these incentives involves the use of judgment related to performance and sales volume estimates that are made based on historical experience and other factors.
69891_12_ITEM8_P22_S4	Sales incentives are accounted for as a reduction of sales and actual amounts ultimately realized may vary from accrued amounts.
69891_12_ITEM8_P23_S0	We operate as a single operating segment for purposes of presenting financial information and evaluating performance.
69891_12_ITEM8_P23_S1	As such, the accompanying consolidated financial statements present financial information in a format that is consistent with the internal financial information used by management.
69891_12_ITEM8_P23_S2	We do not accumulate revenues by product classification and, therefore, it is impractical to present such information.
69891_12_ITEM8_P24_S0	Shipping and handling costs are reported in selling, general and administrative expenses in the accompanying statements of income.
69891_12_ITEM8_P24_S1	Such costs aggregated $45.6 million in Fiscal 2012, $45.1 million in Fiscal 2011 and $43.0 million in Fiscal 2010.
69891_12_ITEM8_P24_S2	Although our classification is consistent with many beverage companies, our gross margin may not be comparable to companies that include shipping and handling costs in cost of sales.
69891_12_ITEM8_P25_S0	Compensation expense for stock-based compensation awards is recognized over the vesting period based on the grant-date fair value estimated using the Black-Scholes model.
69891_12_ITEM8_P26_S0	We record trade receivables at net realizable value, which includes an appropriate allowance for doubtful accounts.
69891_12_ITEM8_P26_S1	We extend credit based on an evaluation of each customer s financial condition, generally without requiring collateral.
69891_12_ITEM8_P27_S0	Exposure to credit losses varies by customer principally due to the financial condition of each customer.
69891_12_ITEM8_P27_S1	We monitor our exposure to credit losses and maintain allowances for anticipated losses based on specific customer circumstances, credit conditions and historical write-offs.

69891_12_ITEM8_P38_S1	CMA, through its personnel, also provides, to the extent possible, the stimulus and creativity to develop an innovative and dynamic persona for the Company, its products and corporate image.
69891_12_ITEM8_P39_S0	In order to fulfill its obligations under the management agreement, CMA employs numerous individuals, whom, acting as a unit, provide management, administrative and creative functions for the Company.
69891_12_ITEM8_P39_S1	The management agreement provides that the Company will pay CMA an annual base fee equal to one percent of the consolidated net sales of the Company, and further provides that the Compensation and Stock Option Committee and the Board of Directors may from time to time award additional incentive compensation to CMA.

69891_12_ITEM8_P56_S0	Our stock-based compensation program is a broad-based program designed to attract and retain employees while also aligning employees interests with the interests of the stockholders.
69891_12_ITEM8_P57_S0	The 1991 Omnibus Incentive Plan (the Omnibus Plan ) provides for compensatory awards consisting of (i) stock options or stock awards for up to 4,800,000 shares of common stock, (ii) stock appreciation rights, dividend equivalents, other stock-based awards in amounts up to 4,800,000 shares of common stock and (iii) performance awards consisting of any combination of the above.
69891_12_ITEM8_P57_S1	The Omnibus Plan is designed to provide an incentive to officers and certain other key employees and consultants by making available to them an opportunity to acquire a proprietary interest or to increase such interest in National Beverage.
69891_12_ITEM8_P58_S0	The number of shares or options which may be issued under stock-based awards to an individual is limited to 1,680,000 during any year.

69891_12_ITEM8_P60_S1	Options may be granted for such consideration as determined by the Board of Directors.
69891_12_ITEM8_P60_S2	The vesting schedule and exercise price of these options are tied to the recipient s ownership level of common stock and the terms generally allow for the reduction in exercise price upon each vesting period.
69891_12_ITEM8_P60_S3	Also, the Board of Directors authorized the issuance of options to purchase up to 50,000 shares of common stock to be issued at the direction of the Chairman.
69891_12_ITEM8_P61_S0	The Key Employee Equity Partnership Program ( KEEP Program ) provides for the granting of stock options to purchase up to 240,000 shares of common stock to key employees, consultants, directors and officers.
69891_12_ITEM8_P61_S1	Participants who purchase shares of stock in the open market receive grants of stock options equal to 50% of the number of shares purchased, up to a maximum of 6,000 shares in any two-year period.
69891_12_ITEM8_P61_S2	Options under the KEEP Program are forfeited in the event of the sale of shares used to acquire such options.
69891_12_ITEM8_P61_S3	Options are granted at an initial exercise price of 60% of the purchase price paid for the shares acquired and the exercise price reduces to the stock par value at the end of the six-year vesting period.
69891_12_ITEM8_P62_S0	We account for stock options under the fair value method of accounting using a Black-Scholes valuation model to estimate the stock option fair value at date of grant.
69891_12_ITEM8_P62_S1	The fair value of stock options is amortized to expense over the vesting period.
69891_12_ITEM8_P62_S2	Stock options granted were 3,000 KEEP shares in Fiscal 2012, 301,500 shares in Fiscal 2011 and 3,000 KEEP shares in Fiscal 2010.
69891_12_ITEM8_P62_S3	The weighted average Black-Scholes fair value assumptions for stock options granted are as follows: weighted average expected life of 8 years for Fiscal 2012, 7.5 years for Fiscal 2011 and 8 years for Fiscal 2010; weighted average expected volatility of 42.9% for Fiscal 2012, 48.6% for Fiscal 2011 and 52.2% for Fiscal 2010; weighted average risk free interest rates of 2.5% for Fiscal 2012, 2.8% for Fiscal 2011 and 3.4% for Fiscal 2010; and expected dividend yield of 5.3% for Fiscal 2012, 4.3% for Fiscal 2011 and 4% for Fiscal 2010.
69891_12_ITEM8_P63_S0	The expected life of stock options was estimated based on historical experience.
69891_12_ITEM8_P63_S1	The expected volatility was estimated based on historical stock prices for a period consistent with the expected life of stock options.
69891_12_ITEM8_P63_S2	The risk free interest rate was based on the U.S. Treasury constant maturity interest rate whose term is consistent with the expected life of stock options.
69891_12_ITEM8_P63_S3	Forfeitures were estimated based on historical experience.

69891_12_ITEM8_P79_S0	We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of National Beverage Corp. as of April 28, 2012 and April 30, 2011 and the related consolidated statements of income, shareholders' equity and cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended April 28, 2012.
69891_12_ITEM8_P79_S1	We also have audited National Beverage Corp. s internal control over financial reporting as of April 28, 2012, based on criteria established in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO).
69891_12_ITEM8_P79_S2	National Beverage Corp. s management is responsible for these financial statements, for maintaining effective internal control over financial reporting and for its assessment of the effectiveness of internal control over financial reporting included in the accompanying Management s Report on Internal Control over Financial Reporting.
69891_12_ITEM8_P79_S3	Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements and an opinion on the Company's internal control over financial reporting based on our audits.
69891_12_ITEM8_P80_S0	We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).
69891_12_ITEM8_P80_S1	Those standards require that we plan and perform the audits to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement and whether effective internal control over financial reporting was maintained in all material respects.
69891_12_ITEM8_P80_S2	Our audits of the financial statements included examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management and evaluating the overall financial statement presentation.
69891_12_ITEM8_P80_S3	Our audit of internal control over financial reporting included obtaining an understanding of internal control over financial reporting, assessing the risk that a material weakness exists and testing and evaluating the design and operating effectiveness of internal control based on the assessed risk.
69891_12_ITEM8_P80_S4	Our audits also included performing such other procedures as we considered necessary in the circumstances.
69891_12_ITEM8_P80_S5	We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinions.
69891_12_ITEM8_P81_S0	A company's internal control over financial reporting is a process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
69891_12_ITEM8_P81_S1	A company's internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that (1) pertain to the maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and dispositions of the assets of the company; (2) provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles and that receipts and expenditures of the company are being made only in accordance with authorizations of management and directors of the company; and (3) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use, or disposition of the company's assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
69891_12_ITEM8_P82_S0	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
69891_12_ITEM8_P82_S1	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
69891_12_ITEM8_P83_S0	In our opinion, the financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of National Beverage Corp. as of April 28, 2012 and April 30, 2011 and the results of its operations and its cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended April 28, 2012, in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.
69891_12_ITEM8_P83_S1	Also in our opinion, National Beverage Corp. maintained, in all material respects, effective internal control over financial reporting as of April 28, 2012, based on criteria established in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO).
69891_12_ITEM9A_P0_S0	As of the end of the period covered by this report, we carried out an evaluation, under the supervision and with the participation of the Company s management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, of the effectiveness of the design and operation of our disclosure controls and procedures (as defined in Rule 13a-15(e) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the Exchange Act )).

69891_12_ITEM9A_P1_S2	Based on that evaluation, our management concluded that our internal control over financial reporting was effective as of April 28, 2012.

69891_13_ITEM1_P0_S0	National Beverage Corp. is an acknowledged leader in the development, manufacturing, marketing and sale of a diverse portfolio of flavored beverage products.
69891_13_ITEM1_P0_S1	Our primary market focus is the United States, but our products are also distributed in Canada, Mexico, the Caribbean, Latin America, the Pacific Rim, Asia, Europe and the Middle East.
69891_13_ITEM1_P1_S0	A holding company for various operating subsidiaries, National Beverage Corp. was incorporated in Delaware in 1985 and began trading as a public company on the NASDAQ Stock Market in 1991.
69891_13_ITEM1_P1_S1	In this report, the terms we, us, our, Company and National Beverage mean National Beverage Corp. and its subsidiaries unless indicated otherwise.
69891_13_ITEM1_P2_S0	Our brands consist of (i) carbonated soft drinks in a variety of flavors as well as regular, diet and reduced-calorie options, and (ii) beverages geared toward the active and health-conscious consumer ( Power+ Brands ), including energy drinks and shots, juices, sparkling waters and enhanced beverages.
69891_13_ITEM1_P2_S1	In addition, we produce soft drinks for certain retailers ( Allied Brands ) that endorse the concept ( Strategic Alliance ) of having our brands and the Allied Brands marketed to produce the effect of enhanced growth of both.
69891_13_ITEM1_P3_S0	We employ a philosophy that emphasizes vertical integration; our vertically-integrated manufacturing model unites the procurement of raw materials and production of concentrates with the manufacture of finished products in our twelve manufacturing facilities.
69891_13_ITEM1_P3_S1	To service a diverse customer base that includes numerous national retailers as well as hundreds of smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts, we have developed a hybrid distribution system that promotes and utilizes customers warehouse distribution facilities and our own direct-store delivery fleet plus the direct-store delivery systems of independent distributors and wholesalers.
69891_13_ITEM1_P4_S0	We believe that the combination of our business strategies and philosophies is key to giving us a greater competitive advantage and differentiating us from our competitors.
69891_13_ITEM1_P5_S0	Fantasy of Flavors Throughout our product lines, we emphasize distinctly flavored beverages.
69891_13_ITEM1_P5_S1	Although cola drinks account for approximately 50% of the soft drink industry s domestic grocery channel volume, colas account for less than 20% of our total volume.
69891_13_ITEM1_P5_S2	In the higher margin convenience store channel, flavors now represent 56% of soft drink sales and are outpacing colas.
69891_13_ITEM1_P5_S3	Our flavor development spans more than 100 years and originated with our flagship brands, Shasta and Faygo , each of which offers more than 50 flavor varieties.
69891_13_ITEM1_P6_S0	Regional Share Dynamics This is our term for the philosophy we employ for the development and support of our brands that have significant regional presence.
69891_13_ITEM1_P6_S1	Because we tailor our marketing and promotion programs by locale, we believe many of our brands enjoy a regional identification that fosters long-term consumer loyalty and make them less vulnerable to competitive substitution.
69891_13_ITEM1_P6_S2	In addition, home-town products often generate more aggressive retailer sponsored promotional activities and receive media exposure through community activities rather than costly national advertising.
69891_13_ITEM1_P7_S0	We believe that consumers demand value as the purchase default option in volatile economic times, and we are intent on producing and developing products of the highest quality that appeal to the value expectations of the family consumer.
69891_13_ITEM1_P7_S1	We believe we can leverage our cost-effective manufacturing and distribution systems, and our efficient regionally focused marketing programs, to profitably deliver products to the consumer at a lower price-point than our national competitors.
69891_13_ITEM1_P8_S0	Creative Agility In a beverage industry that is dominated by the cola giants , we pride ourselves on our ability to respond faster and more creatively to consumer trends than many of our competitors which are burdened by distribution complexity and legacy costs.
69891_13_ITEM1_P8_S1	We strive to build long-term brand value by developing creative marketing programs, propriety flavors and distinctive packaging.
69891_13_ITEM1_P8_S2	During the past two years, we have introduced numerous new flavors or package sizes and have won many package design awards.
69891_13_ITEM1_P8_S3	We continue to develop products and package sizes designed to expand distribution in the higher-margin convenience store channel.
69891_13_ITEM1_P8_S4	We believe that the most dynamic validation of our strategy is our competitors efforts to replicate our creative business model.
69891_13_ITEM1_P9_S0	Lifestyle Focus In recent years, we have honed our focus on developing healthier and functional beverages in response to a global shift in consumer buying habits.
69891_13_ITEM1_P9_S1	As health and wellness awareness grows, consumers are turning to drinks with reduced calories, wholesome ingredients and efficacy to meet their specific lifestyle needs.
69891_13_ITEM1_P9_S2	We are committed to tailoring the variety and types of beverages in our portfolio to satisfy changing preferences of an increasingly diverse mix of consumers.
69891_13_ITEM1_P10_S0	Our wide variety of brands meets the demands of multiple consumer groups:
69891_13_ITEM1_P11_S0	Established more than 120 years ago and distributed nationally, Shasta is recognized to be a bottling industry pioneer and innovator.
69891_13_ITEM1_P11_S1	As our largest volume brand, Shasta features multiple flavors, including products targeted to the growing Hispanic and other ethnic markets, and continues to earn consumer loyalty by delivering value, convenience and unique tastes such as California Dreamin , Very Cherry Twist and Fiesta Punch.
69891_13_ITEM1_P12_S0	More than 100 years old, Faygo products are primarily distributed east of the Mississippi River and include numerous unique flavors including RedPop, Moon Mist and Rock n Rye .
69891_13_ITEM1_P12_S1	We also produce and market Ritz soft drinks and seltzers, primarily in the southeastern U.S., distribute Big Shot in New Orleans and surrounding areas, and offer St. Nick s soft drinks during the holiday season.
69891_13_ITEM1_P13_S0	With all natural ingredients, LaCroix has been outpacing the growing sparkling water segment that is fast becoming the alternative to the more typical carbonated soft drink.
69891_13_ITEM1_P13_S1	Containing no calories, sodium or caffeine, LaCroix has the support of major national chains and is the top- selling canned sparkling water in the U.S. as well as the number one domestically-produced sparkling water.
69891_13_ITEM1_P13_S2	New themes of LaCroix with new packages and ingredient concepts are being designed and tested to be sold in new areas for the retailer not presently utilized for soft drinks.
69891_13_ITEM1_P13_S3	Other products we deliver the health-conscious consumer include Clear Fruit , a clean, crisp, all natural non-carbonated beverage; and Crystal Bay , a zero-calorie combination of sparkling water and lively fruit flavors.
69891_13_ITEM1_P14_S0	Rip It energy fuel is available nationally in 19 flavors including five sugar-free and three non-carbonated varieties, and is a dominant player in the dollar-store channel.
69891_13_ITEM1_P14_S1	Building on the success of Rip It, we offer two-ounce Rip It Shots in six flavors, including Tribute a new blend of active mandarin and live wild lime.
69891_13_ITEM1_P14_S2	For consumers seeking vitamin-enhanced hydration, we offer Mega Sport in four reinvigorating flavors.
69891_13_ITEM1_P15_S0	Everfresh , Home Juice and Mr. Pure 100% fresh juice and juice-added products and non-carbonated fruit drinks are available in over 30 flavors including Blueberry Pomegranate, Kiwi Strawberry and Pineapple Mango.
69891_13_ITEM1_P15_S1	Originating in the Midwest over 50 years ago, these brands feature unique glass packaging targeted primarily for single-serve consumption.
69891_13_ITEM1_P16_S0	Our Ohana line of fruit drinks, lemonades and teas quenches thirst without carbonation.
69891_13_ITEM1_P16_S1	We have been successfully expanding to new geographic areas through both independent and Company-owned distribution facilities.
69891_13_ITEM1_P17_S0	Our twelve manufacturing facilities are strategically located near major metropolitan markets across the continental United States.
69891_13_ITEM1_P17_S1	The locations of our plants enable us to efficiently manufacture and distribute beverages to substantially all geographic markets in the United States, including 22 of the top 25 metropolitan statistical areas.
69891_13_ITEM1_P17_S2	Each manufacturing facility is generally equipped to produce both canned and bottled beverage products in a variety of package sizes.
69891_13_ITEM1_P17_S3	We utilize numerous package types and sizes, including cans ranging from eight to sixteen ounces and bottles ranging from seven ounces to three liters.
69891_13_ITEM1_P18_S0	We believe that the innovative and controlled vertical integration of our bottling facilities provides an advantage over certain of our competitors that rely upon independent third party bottlers to manufacture and market their products.
69891_13_ITEM1_P18_S1	Since we control the national production, distribution and marketing of our brands, we believe we can more effectively manage product quality and customer service and respond quickly to changing market conditions.
69891_13_ITEM1_P19_S0	We produce a substantial portion of the flavor concentrates used in our branded products.
69891_13_ITEM1_P19_S1	By controlling our own formulas throughout our bottling network, we can manufacture our products in accordance with uniform quality standards while tailoring flavors to regional taste preferences.
69891_13_ITEM1_P19_S2	We believe that the combination of a Company-owned bottling network, together with uniform standards for packaging, formulations and customer service, provides us with a strategic advantage in servicing national retailers and mass-merchandisers.
69891_13_ITEM1_P19_S3	We also maintain research and development laboratories at multiple locations.
69891_13_ITEM1_P19_S4	These laboratories continually test products for compliance with our strict quality control standards as well as conduct research for new products and flavors.
69891_13_ITEM1_P20_S0	We utilize a hybrid distribution system to deliver our products through three primary distribution channels: take-home, convenience and food-service.
69891_13_ITEM1_P21_S0	The take-home distribution channel consists of national and regional grocery stores, warehouse clubs, mass-merchandisers, wholesalers and dollar stores.
69891_13_ITEM1_P21_S1	We distribute our products to this channel through the warehouse distribution system and the direct-store delivery system.
69891_13_ITEM1_P22_S0	Under the warehouse distribution system, products are shipped from our manufacturing facilities to the retailer s centralized distribution centers and then distributed by the retailer to each of its outlet locations with other goods.
69891_13_ITEM1_P22_S1	Products sold through the direct-store delivery system are distributed directly to the customer s retail outlets by our direct-store delivery fleet and by independent distributors.
69891_13_ITEM1_P23_S0	We distribute our products to the convenience channel through our own direct-store delivery fleet and those of independent distributors.
69891_13_ITEM1_P24_S0	The convenience channel consists of convenience stores, gas stations and other smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts.
69891_13_ITEM1_P24_S1	Because of the higher retail prices and margins that typically prevail, we have undertaken several measures to expand convenience channel distribution.
69891_13_ITEM1_P24_S2	These include development of products, packaging and graphics specifically targeted to this market.
69891_13_ITEM1_P25_S0	Our food-service division distributes products to independent, specialized distributors who sell to hospitals, schools, military bases, airlines, hotels and food-service wholesalers.
69891_13_ITEM1_P25_S1	Also, our Company-owned direct-store delivery fleet distributes products to certain schools and other food-service customers.
69891_13_ITEM1_P26_S0	Our take-home, convenience and food-service operations use vending machines and glass-door coolers as marketing and promotional tools for our brands.
69891_13_ITEM1_P26_S1	We provide vending machines and coolers on a placement or purchase basis to our customers.
69891_13_ITEM1_P26_S2	We believe vending and cooler equipment increases beverage sales, enhances brand awareness and develops brand loyalty.
69891_13_ITEM1_P27_S0	We sell and market our products through an internal sales force as well as specialized broker networks.
69891_13_ITEM1_P27_S1	Our sales force is organized to serve a specific market, focusing on one or more geographic territories, distribution channels or product lines.
69891_13_ITEM1_P27_S2	We believe this focus allows our sales group to provide high level, responsive service and support to our customers and markets.
69891_13_ITEM1_P28_S0	The emphasis of our sales and marketing programs is to maintain and enhance consumer brand recognition and loyalty, typically through a combination of regional advertising, special event marketing, endorsements, sponsorships and social media, along with consumer coupon distribution and product sampling.
69891_13_ITEM1_P28_S1	We retain advertising agencies to assist with media advertising programs for our brands.
69891_13_ITEM1_P28_S2	Additionally, we offer numerous promotional programs to retail customers, including cooperative advertising support, in-store advertising materials and other incentives.
69891_13_ITEM1_P28_S3	These elements allow us to tailor our marketing and advertising programs to meet local and regional economic conditions and demographics.
69891_13_ITEM1_P28_S4	Additionally, we sponsor special holiday promotions which feature St. Nick s soft drink and special holiday flavors and packaging.
69891_13_ITEM1_P29_S0	Our centralized procurement group maintains relationships with numerous suppliers of raw materials and packaging goods.
69891_13_ITEM1_P29_S1	By consolidating the purchasing function for our manufacturing facilities, we believe we are able to procure more competitive arrangements with our suppliers, thereby allowing us to compete as a low-cost producer of beverages.
69891_13_ITEM1_P30_S0	The products we produce and sell are made from various materials including sweeteners, juice concentrates, carbon dioxide, water, glass and plastic bottles, aluminum cans and ends, paper, cartons and closures.
69891_13_ITEM1_P30_S1	Most of our low-calorie soft drink products use sucralose, aspartame, stevia or Acesulfame-K. We manufacture a substantial portion of our flavor concentrates and purchase remaining raw materials from multiple suppliers.
69891_13_ITEM1_P31_S0	Substantially all of the materials and ingredients we purchase are presently available from several suppliers, although strikes, weather conditions, utility shortages, governmental control or regulations, national emergencies, price or supply fluctuations or other events outside our control could adversely affect the supply of specific materials.
69891_13_ITEM1_P31_S1	A significant portion of our raw material purchases, including aluminum cans, plastic bottles, high fructose corn syrup, corrugated packaging and juice concentrates, are derived from commodities.
69891_13_ITEM1_P31_S2	Therefore, pricing and availability tend to fluctuate based upon worldwide market conditions.
69891_13_ITEM1_P31_S3	Our ability to recover increased costs through higher pricing may be limited by the competitive environment in which we operate.
69891_13_ITEM1_P31_S4	In certain cases, we may elect to enter into multi-year agreements for the supply of these materials with one or more suppliers, the terms of which may include variable or fixed pricing, minimum purchase quantities and/or the requirement to purchase all supplies for specified locations.
69891_13_ITEM1_P31_S5	Additionally, we use derivative financial instruments to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in certain raw material costs.
69891_13_ITEM1_P32_S0	The majority of our sales are seasonal with the highest volume typically realized during the summer months.
69891_13_ITEM1_P32_S1	We have sufficient production capacity to meet seasonal increases without maintaining significant quantities of inventory in anticipation of periods of peak demand.
69891_13_ITEM1_P32_S2	Additionally, our sales can be influenced by weather conditions.
69891_13_ITEM1_P33_S0	The beverage industry is highly competitive and our competitive position varies in each of our market areas.
69891_13_ITEM1_P33_S1	Our products compete with many varieties of liquid refreshment, including soft drinks, water products, juices, fruit drinks, powdered drinks, coffees, teas, energy drinks, sports drinks, dairy-based drinks, functional beverages and various other nonalcoholic beverages.
69891_13_ITEM1_P33_S2	We compete with bottlers and distributors of national, regional and private label products.
69891_13_ITEM1_P33_S3	Several competitors, including the two that dominate the soft drink industry, PepsiCo and The Coca-Cola Company, have greater financial resources than we have and aggressive promotion of their products can adversely affect sales of our brands.
69891_13_ITEM1_P34_S0	Principal methods of competition in the beverage industry are price and promotional activity, advertising and marketing programs, point-of-sale merchandising, retail space management, customer service, product differentiation, packaging innovations and distribution methods.
69891_13_ITEM1_P34_S1	We believe our Company differentiates itself through a diversified product portfolio, strong regional brand recognition, innovative flavor variety, attractive packaging, efficient distribution methods, specialized advertising and, for some product lines, value pricing.
69891_13_ITEM1_P35_S0	We own numerous trademarks for our brands that are significant to our business.
69891_13_ITEM1_P35_S1	We intend to continue to maintain all registrations of our significant trademarks and use the trademarks in the operation of our businesses.
69891_13_ITEM1_P36_S0	The production, distribution and sale of our products in the United States are subject to the Federal Food, Drug and Cosmetic Act; the Dietary Supplement Health and Education Act of 1994; the Occupational Safety and Health Act; the Lanham Act; various environmental statutes; and various other federal, state and local statutes regulating the production, transportation, sale, safety, advertising, labeling and ingredients of such products.
69891_13_ITEM1_P36_S1	We believe that we are in compliance, in all material respects, with such existing legislation.
69891_13_ITEM1_P37_S0	Certain states and localities prohibit the sale of certain beverages unless a deposit or tax is charged for containers.
69891_13_ITEM1_P37_S1	These requirements vary by each jurisdiction.
69891_13_ITEM1_P37_S2	Similar legislation has been proposed in certain other states and localities, as well as by Congress.
69891_13_ITEM1_P37_S3	We are unable to predict whether such legislation will be enacted or what impact its enactment would have on our business, financial condition or results of operations.
69891_13_ITEM1_P38_S0	All of our facilities in the United States are subject to federal, state and local environmental laws and regulations.
69891_13_ITEM1_P38_S1	Compliance with these provisions has not had any material adverse effect on our financial or competitive position.
69891_13_ITEM1_P38_S2	We believe that our current practices and procedures for the control and disposition of toxic or hazardous substances comply in all material respects with applicable law.
69891_13_ITEM1_P38_S3	Compliance with or violation of any current or future regulations and legislation could require material expenditures or have a material adverse effect on our financial results.
69891_13_ITEM1_P39_S0	As of April 27, 2013, we employed approximately 1,200 people, of which approximately 300 are covered by collective bargaining agreements.
69891_13_ITEM1_P40_S0	We believe that relations with our employees are generally good.

69891_13_ITEM1A_P0_S0	In addition to other information in this Annual Report on Form 10-K, the following risk factors should be considered carefully in evaluating the Company s business.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P0_S1	Our business, financial condition and results of operations could be materially and adversely affected by any of these risks.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P0_S2	Additional risks and uncertainties, including risks and uncertainties not presently known to the Company, or that the Company currently deems immaterial, may also impair our business and results of operations.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P1_S0	Changes in consumer preferences and taste.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P1_S1	There has been an increasing focus on health and wellness by beverage consumers, which may reduce demand for caloric carbonated soft drinks and increase the consumption of products perceived to deliver health, wellness and/or functionality.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P2_S0	If we do not adequately anticipate and react to changing demographics, consumer trends, health concerns and product preferences, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P3_S0	The beverage industry is extremely competitive.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P3_S1	Our products compete with a broad range of beverage products, most of which are manufactured and distributed by companies with substantially greater financial, marketing and distribution resources.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P3_S2	In order to generate future revenues and profits, we must continue to sell products that appeal to our customers and consumers.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P3_S3	Discounting and other actions by our competitors may make it more difficult to sustain revenues and profits.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P4_S0	Our retail customer base has been consolidating over the last several years resulting in fewer customers with increased purchasing power.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P4_S1	This increased purchasing power can limit our ability to increase pricing for our products with certain of our customers.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P4_S2	Our inability to meet the demands of our larger customers could lead to a loss of business and adversely affect our financial results.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P5_S0	The production of our products is dependent on certain raw materials, including aluminum, resin, corn, linerboard and fruit juice.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P5_S1	In addition, the production and distribution of our products is dependent on energy sources, including natural gas, fuel and electricity.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P5_S2	These items are subject to price volatility caused by numerous factors.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P5_S3	Commodity price increases ultimately result in a corresponding increase in the cost of raw materials and energy.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P5_S4	We may be limited in our ability to pass these increases on to our customers or may incur a loss in sales volume to the extent price increases are taken.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P5_S5	In addition, strikes, weather conditions, governmental controls, national emergencies, natural disasters, supply shortages or other events could affect our continued supply of raw materials and energy.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P5_S6	If raw materials or energy costs increase, or the availability is limited, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P6_S0	Our business and properties are subject to various federal, state and local laws and regulations, including those governing the production, packaging, quality, labeling and distribution of beverage products.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P6_S1	In addition, various governmental agencies have considered imposing taxes on soft drinks and other sugar-sweetened beverages, including those sweetened with high fructose corn syrup.
69891_13_ITEM1A_P6_S2	New laws or regulations or changes in existing laws or regulations could negatively affect our financial results through lower sales or higher operating costs.
69891_13_ITEM2_P0_S0	Our principal properties include twelve manufacturing facilities located in ten states, which aggregate approximately two million square feet.
69891_13_ITEM2_P0_S1	We own ten manufacturing facilities in the following states: California (2), Georgia, Kansas, Michigan (2), Ohio, Texas, Utah and Washington.
69891_13_ITEM2_P0_S2	Two manufacturing facilities, located in Maryland and Florida, are leased subject to agreements that expire through 2020.
69891_13_ITEM2_P0_S3	We believe our facilities are generally in good condition and sufficient to meet our present needs.
69891_13_ITEM2_P1_S0	The production of beverages is capital intensive but is not characterized by rapid technological change.
69891_13_ITEM2_P1_S1	The technological advances that have occurred have generally been of an incremental cost-saving nature, such as the industry s conversion to lighter weight containers or improved blending processes that enhance ingredient yields.
69891_13_ITEM2_P1_S2	We are not aware of any anticipated industry-wide changes in technology that would adversely impact our current physical production capacity or cost of production.
69891_13_ITEM2_P2_S0	We own and lease trucks, vans and automobiles used in the sale, delivery and distribution of our products.
69891_13_ITEM2_P2_S1	In addition, we lease office and warehouse space, transportation equipment, office equipment and certain manufacturing equipment.
69891_13_ITEM3_P0_S0	From time to time, we are a party to various litigation matters arising in the ordinary course of business.
69891_13_ITEM3_P0_S1	We do not expect the ultimate disposition of such matters to have a material adverse effect on our consolidated financial position or results of operations.
