69891_14_ITEM8_P44_S0	The Company is a party to a management agreement with Corporate Management Advisors, Inc. ( CMA ), a corporation owned by our Chairman and Chief Executive Officer.
69891_14_ITEM8_P44_S1	This agreement was originated in 1991 for the efficient use of management of two public companies at the time.
69891_14_ITEM8_P44_S2	In 1994, one of those public entities, through a merger, no longer was managed in this manner.
69891_14_ITEM8_P45_S0	Under the terms of the agreement, CMA provides, subject to the direction and supervision of the Board of Directors of the Company, (i) senior corporate functions (including supervision of the Company s financial, legal, executive recruitment, internal audit and management information systems departments) as well as the services of a Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, and (ii) services in connection with acquisitions, dispositions and financings by the Company, including identifying and profiling acquisition candidates, negotiating and structuring potential transactions and arranging financing for any such transaction.
69891_14_ITEM8_P45_S1	CMA, through its personnel, also provides, to the extent possible, the stimulus and creativity to develop an innovative and dynamic persona for the Company, its products and corporate image.
69891_14_ITEM8_P46_S0	In order to fulfill its obligations under the management agreement, CMA employs numerous individuals, whom, acting as a unit, provide management, administrative and creative functions for the Company.
69891_14_ITEM8_P46_S1	The management agreement provides that the Company will pay CMA an annual base fee equal to one percent of the consolidated net sales of the Company, and further provides that the Compensation and Stock Option Committee and the Board of Directors may from time to time award additional incentive compensation to CMA.
69891_14_ITEM8_P46_S2	The Board of Directors on numerous occasions contemplated incentive compensation and, while shareholder value has increased over 2,000% since the inception of this agreement, no incentive compensation has been paid.
69891_14_ITEM8_P47_S0	We incurred management fees to CMA of $6.4 million for Fiscal 2014, $6.6 million for Fiscal 2013 and $6.3 million for Fiscal 2012.

69891_14_ITEM8_P48_S0	From time to time, we enter into aluminum swap contracts to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in the cost of aluminum cans.
69891_14_ITEM8_P48_S1	Such financial instruments are designated and accounted for as a cash flow hedge.
69891_14_ITEM8_P48_S2	Accordingly, gains or losses attributable to the effective portion of the cash flow hedge are reported in Accumulated Other Comprehensive Income (Loss) ( AOCI ) and reclassified into earnings through cost of sales in the period in which the hedged transaction affects earnings.

69891_14_ITEM8_P64_S0	Our stock-based compensation program is a broad-based program designed to attract and retain employees while also aligning employees interests with the interests of the stockholders.
69891_14_ITEM8_P65_S0	The 1991 Omnibus Incentive Plan (the Omnibus Plan ) provides for compensatory awards consisting of (i) stock options or stock awards for up to 4,800,000 shares of common stock, (ii) stock appreciation rights, dividend equivalents, other stock-based awards in amounts up to 4,800,000 shares of common stock and (iii) performance awards consisting of any combination of the above.
69891_14_ITEM8_P65_S1	The Omnibus Plan is designed to provide an incentive to officers and certain other key employees and consultants by making available to them an opportunity to acquire a proprietary interest or to increase such interest in National Beverage.
69891_14_ITEM8_P66_S0	The number of shares or options which may be issued under stock-based awards to an individual is limited to 1,680,000 during any year.
69891_14_ITEM8_P66_S1	Awards may be granted for no cash consideration or such minimal cash consideration as may be required by law.
69891_14_ITEM8_P67_S0	Options generally have an exercise price equal to the fair market value of our common stock on the date of grant, vest over a five-year period and expire after ten years.
69891_14_ITEM8_P68_S0	The Special Stock Option Plan provides for the issuance of stock options to purchase up to an aggregate of 1,800,000 shares of common stock.
69891_14_ITEM8_P68_S1	Options may be granted for such consideration as determined by the Board of Directors.
69891_14_ITEM8_P68_S2	The vesting schedule and exercise price of these options are tied to the recipient s ownership level of common stock and the terms generally allow for the reduction in exercise price upon each vesting period.
69891_14_ITEM8_P68_S3	Also, the Board of Directors authorized the issuance of options to purchase up to 50,000 shares of common stock to be issued at the direction of the Chairman.
69891_14_ITEM8_P69_S0	The Key Employee Equity Partnership Program ( KEEP Program ) provides for the granting of stock options to purchase up to 240,000 shares of common stock to key employees, consultants, directors and officers.
69891_14_ITEM8_P69_S1	Participants who purchase shares of stock in the open market receive grants of stock options equal to 50% of the number of shares purchased, up to a maximum of 6,000 shares in any two-year period.
69891_14_ITEM8_P69_S2	Options under the KEEP Program are forfeited in the event of the sale of shares used to acquire such options.
69891_14_ITEM8_P69_S3	Options are granted at an initial exercise price of 60% of the purchase price paid for the shares acquired and the exercise price reduces to the stock par value at the end of the six-year vesting period.
69891_14_ITEM8_P70_S0	We account for stock options under the fair value method of accounting using a Black-Scholes valuation model to estimate the stock option fair value at date of grant.
69891_14_ITEM8_P70_S1	The fair value of stock options is amortized to expense over the vesting period.
69891_14_ITEM8_P70_S2	Stock options granted were 5,245 KEEP shares in Fiscal 2014, 2,000 KEEP shares in Fiscal 2013 and 3,000 KEEP shares in Fiscal 2012.
69891_14_ITEM8_P70_S3	The weighted average Black-Scholes fair value assumptions for stock options granted are as follows: weighted average expected life of 8 years for Fiscal 2014, 8 years for Fiscal 2013 and 8 years for Fiscal 2012; weighted average expected volatility of 35.8% for Fiscal 2014, 38.1% for Fiscal 2013 and 42.9% for Fiscal 2012; weighted average risk free interest rates of 1.9% for Fiscal 2014, 1.6% for Fiscal 2013 and 2.5% for Fiscal 2012; and expected dividend yield of 4.6% for Fiscal 2014, 5.0% for Fiscal 2013 and 5.3% for Fiscal 2012.
69891_14_ITEM8_P71_S0	The expected life of stock options was estimated based on historical experience.
69891_14_ITEM8_P71_S1	The expected volatility was estimated based on historical stock prices for a period consistent with the expected life of stock options.
69891_14_ITEM8_P71_S2	The risk free interest rate was based on the U.S. Treasury constant maturity interest rate whose term is consistent with the expected life of stock options.
69891_14_ITEM8_P71_S3	Forfeitures were estimated based on historical experience.

69891_14_ITEM8_P90_S0	We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of National Beverage Corp. as of May 3, 2014 and April 27, 2013 and the related consolidated statements of income, comprehensive income, shareholders equity and cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended May 3, 2014.
69891_14_ITEM8_P90_S1	We also have audited National Beverage Corp. s internal control over financial reporting as of May 3, 2014, based on criteria established in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO) in 1992.
69891_14_ITEM8_P90_S2	National Beverage Corp. s management is responsible for these financial statements, for maintaining effective internal control over financial reporting and for its assessment of the effectiveness of internal control over financial reporting included in the accompanying Management s Report on Internal Control over Financial Reporting.
69891_14_ITEM8_P90_S3	Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements and an opinion on the Company s internal control over financial reporting based on our audits.
69891_14_ITEM8_P91_S0	We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).
69891_14_ITEM8_P91_S1	Those standards require that we plan and perform the audits to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement and whether effective internal control over financial reporting was maintained in all material respects.
69891_14_ITEM8_P91_S2	Our audits of the financial statements included examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management and evaluating the overall financial statement presentation.
69891_14_ITEM8_P91_S3	Our audit of internal control over financial reporting included obtaining an understanding of internal control over financial reporting, assessing the risk that a material weakness exists and testing and evaluating the design and operating effectiveness of internal control based on the assessed risk.
69891_14_ITEM8_P91_S4	Our audits also included performing such other procedures as we considered necessary in the circumstances.
69891_14_ITEM8_P91_S5	We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinions.
69891_14_ITEM8_P92_S0	A company s internal control over financial reporting is a process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
69891_14_ITEM8_P92_S1	A company s internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that (1) pertain to the maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and dispositions of the assets of the company; (2) provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles and that receipts and expenditures of the company are being made only in accordance with authorizations of management and directors of the company; and (3) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use, or disposition of the company s assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
69891_14_ITEM8_P93_S0	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
69891_14_ITEM8_P93_S1	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
69891_14_ITEM8_P94_S0	In our opinion, the consolidated financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of National Beverage Corp. as of May 3, 2014 and April 27, 2013 and the results of their operations and their cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended May 3, 2014, in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.
69891_14_ITEM8_P94_S1	Also in our opinion, National Beverage Corp. maintained, in all material respects, effective internal control over financial reporting as of May 3, 2014, based on criteria established in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO) in 1992.
69891_14_ITEM9A_P0_S0	Disclosure Controls and Procedures As of the end of the period covered by this Annual Report on Form 10-K, we carried out an evaluation, under the supervision and with the participation of the Company s management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, of the effectiveness of the design and operation of our disclosure controls and procedures (as defined in Rule 13a-15(e) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the Exchange Act )).
69891_14_ITEM9A_P0_S1	Based upon that evaluation, the Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer concluded that our disclosure controls and procedures were effective to ensure information required to be disclosed by us in reports we file or submit under the Exchange Act is (1) recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified in SEC rules and forms and (2) accumulated and communicated to our management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, to allow timely decisions regarding required disclosure.
69891_14_ITEM9A_P1_S0	Our management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting, as such term is defined in Rule 13a-15(f) of the Exchange Act.
69891_14_ITEM9A_P1_S1	Under the supervision and with the participation of our management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, we conducted an evaluation of the effectiveness of our internal control over financial reporting based on the framework in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission in 1992.
69891_14_ITEM9A_P1_S2	Based on that evaluation, our management concluded that our internal control over financial reporting was effective as of May 3, 2014.
69891_14_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Management recognizes that there are inherent limitations in the effectiveness of any internal control over financial reporting, including the possibility of human error and the circumvention or overriding of internal control.
69891_14_ITEM9A_P2_S1	Accordingly, even effective internal control over financial reporting can provide only reasonable assurance with respect to financial statement preparation.
69891_14_ITEM9A_P2_S2	Further, because of changes in conditions, the effectiveness of internal control may vary over time.

69891_14_ITEM15_P27_S0	In connection with the Annual Report of National Beverage Corp. (the Company ) on Form 10-K for the period ended May 3, 2014 (the Report ), I, George R. 69891_15_ITEM1_P0_S0	Currently celebrating its 30 th anniversary, National Beverage Corp. is an acknowledged leader in the development, manufacturing, marketing and sale of a diverse portfolio of flavored beverage products.
69891_15_ITEM1_P0_S1	Our primary market focus is the United States, but our products are also distributed in Canada, Mexico, the Caribbean, Latin America, the Pacific Rim, Asia, and Europe.
69891_15_ITEM1_P1_S0	A holding company for various operating subsidiaries, National Beverage Corp. was incorporated in Delaware in 1985 and began trading as a public company on the NASDAQ Stock Market in 1991.
69891_15_ITEM1_P1_S1	In this report, the terms we, us, our, Company and National Beverage mean National Beverage Corp. and its subsidiaries unless indicated otherwise.
69891_15_ITEM1_P2_S0	Our brands consist of (i) beverages geared toward the active and health-conscious consumer ( Power+ Brands ), including sparkling waters, energy drinks and shots, juices, and enhanced beverages, and (ii) Carbonated Soft Drinks in a variety of flavors including regular, sugar-free and reduced-calorie options.
69891_15_ITEM1_P2_S1	In addition, we produce soft drinks for certain retailers ( Allied Brands ) that endorse the Strategic Alliance concept of having our brands and Allied Brands marketed to effectuate enhanced growth of both.
69891_15_ITEM1_P3_S0	We employ a philosophy that emphasizes vertical integration; our manufacturing model integrates the procurement of raw materials and production of concentrates with the manufacture of finished products in our twelve manufacturing facilities.
69891_15_ITEM1_P3_S1	To service a diverse customer base that includes numerous national retailers as well as thousands of smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts, we have developed a hybrid distribution system that promotes and utilizes customer warehouse distribution facilities and our own direct-store delivery fleet plus the direct-store delivery systems of independent distributors and wholesalers.
69891_15_ITEM1_P4_S0	We believe that the combination of our business strategies and philosophies is key to giving us a greater competitive advantage and differentiating us from our competitors.
69891_15_ITEM1_P4_S1	These points of differentiation include the following:
69891_15_ITEM1_P5_S0	Lifestyle Focus We focus on developing healthier and functional beverages in response to a global shift in consumer buying habits.
69891_15_ITEM1_P5_S1	As health and wellness awareness grows, consumers are turning to drinks with reduced calories, wholesome ingredients and efficacy to meet their specific lifestyle needs.
69891_15_ITEM1_P5_S2	We are committed to tailoring the variety and types of beverages in our portfolio to satisfy changing preferences of an increasingly diverse mix of crossover consumers a growing group who desire a change from Carbonated Soft Drinks and other artificially flavored, artificially sweetened beverages.
69891_15_ITEM1_P6_S0	Fantasy of Flavors Throughout our product lines, we emphasize distinctly flavored beverages.
69891_15_ITEM1_P7_S0	Although cola drinks account for approximately 49% of the soft drink industry s domestic grocery channel volume, colas account for less than 20% of our total volume.
69891_15_ITEM1_P7_S1	In the higher margin convenience store channel, flavors represent 55% of soft drink sales and are outpacing colas.
69891_15_ITEM1_P7_S2	Our flavor development spans more than 125 years and originated with our flagship brands, Shasta and Faygo , each of which offers more than 30 flavor varieties.
69891_15_ITEM1_P8_S0	Regional Share Dynamics This is our term for the philosophy we employ for the development and support of our brands that have significant regional presence.
69891_15_ITEM1_P8_S1	Because we tailor our marketing and promotion programs by locale, we believe many of our brands enjoy a regional identification that fosters long-term consumer loyalty and make them less vulnerable to competitive substitution.
69891_15_ITEM1_P8_S2	In addition, home-town products often generate more aggressive retailer sponsored promotional activities and receive media exposure through community activities rather than costly national advertising.
69891_15_ITEM1_P9_S0	We believe that consumers demand value as the purchase default option in volatile economic times, and we are intent on producing and developing products of the highest quality that appeal to the value expectations of the family consumer.
69891_15_ITEM1_P9_S1	We believe we can leverage our cost-effective manufacturing and distribution systems, and our efficient regionally focused marketing programs, to profitably deliver products to the consumer at a lower price-point than our national competitors.
69891_15_ITEM1_P10_S0	Creative Agility In a beverage industry that is dominated by the cola giants , we pride ourselves on our ability to respond faster and more creatively to consumer trends than many of our competitors who are burdened by distribution complexity and legacy costs.
69891_15_ITEM1_P10_S1	We strive to build long-term brand value by developing creative marketing programs, propriety flavors and distinctive packaging.
69891_15_ITEM1_P10_S2	In recent years, we have introduced numerous new flavors or package sizes and have won many package design awards.
69891_15_ITEM1_P10_S3	We continue to develop products and package sizes designed to expand distribution.
69891_15_ITEM1_P10_S4	We believe that the most dynamic validation of our strategy is our competitors efforts to replicate our creative business model.
69891_15_ITEM1_P11_S0	The National Beverage Corp. brand portfolio contains a wide variety of beverages to meet consumer needs in a multitude of market segments.
69891_15_ITEM1_P11_S1	National Beverage employs its flavor expertise with beverage offerings including, but not limited to, the following non-alcoholic beverage segments:
69891_15_ITEM1_P12_S0	La Croix 100% all natural LaCroix Sparkling Water is setting the pace in the Sparkling Water category that is fast becoming the alternative to traditional carbonated soda.
69891_15_ITEM1_P12_S1	With zero calories, zero sweeteners and zero sodium, the innocence of LaCroix has the support of major national chains and is the top-selling domestic Sparkling Water packaged in cans.
69891_15_ITEM1_P13_S0	naturally refresh in tall 12 oz.
69891_15_ITEM1_P13_S1	Brilliant graphics, robust aroma, naturally essenced and premium-priced, C rate is a trendsetting addition to a brand that is the healthy alternative for trend-forward consumers.
69891_15_ITEM1_P14_S0	NiCola by LaCroix, a new innovative sparkling water with the essence and flavor of cola, is innocent of calories, sodium, sweetener or any ingredient that the health-conscious consumer avoids.
69891_15_ITEM1_P14_S1	Since its initial Chicago launch in October 2014, NiCola has received positive response from cola and diet cola drinkers looking to crossover to a beverage that complements a healthier lifestyle.
69891_15_ITEM1_P15_S0	Additional LaCroix themes are in development and feature unique packaging, ground-breaking flavor concepts, and a go-to-market strategy designed to provide additional placements within the retail environment outside the traditional grocery shelf.
69891_15_ITEM1_P16_S0	Rip It Rip It energy fuel is the flavor innovator in the growing energy category with 14 unique flavors including six sugar free, bringing variety and value to the widening consumer base.
69891_15_ITEM1_P16_S1	Rip It Tribute themed energy is a successful military inspired addition to the lineup with the latest addition Tribute CYP-X Orange Cr me.
69891_15_ITEM1_P16_S2	Building on the flavor tradition of original Rip It, a 2 oz. sugar free shot version with seven flavors is marketed through our distribution system in multiple displayable package configurations.
69891_15_ITEM1_P17_S0	Everfresh 100% juice and juice drinks are available in more than 35 flavors, from such classics as Orange, Cranberry and flavored lemonades to exotics that include Premium Papaya and Pineapple Mango.
69891_15_ITEM1_P18_S0	Originating in the Midwest, the Everfresh signature package is a hot-filled, 16 oz. glass bottle primarily for single-serve consumption.
69891_15_ITEM1_P18_S1	Additional consumer - friendly packages range from 10 oz.
69891_15_ITEM1_P19_S0	Everfresh Premier Varietals , a unique theme from Everfresh, is positioned as a stand-alone brand for display in the produce section of supermarkets.
69891_15_ITEM1_P19_S1	Everfresh Premier Varietals is a premium line of 100% natural apple juice from a variety of apples specific to the taste of the varietal, such as Granny Smith, McIntosh, Honey Crisp, Golden Delicious, Fuji and Pink Lady.
69891_15_ITEM1_P19_S2	Premier Varietals are packaged in award-winning 12 oz.
69891_15_ITEM1_P19_S3	glass bottles with decorative tamper-evident neck seals.
69891_15_ITEM1_P20_S0	More than 125 years old and distributed nationally, Shasta is recognized as a bottling industry pioneer and innovator.
69891_15_ITEM1_P20_S1	As our largest volume brand, Shasta features multiple flavors, including products targeted to the growing Hispanic and other ethnic markets, and continues to earn consumer loyalty by delivering value, convenience and such unique tastes as California Dreamin , Very Cherry Twist and Fiesta Punch.
69891_15_ITEM1_P20_S2	Honoring its origin as a sparkling water company, Shasta will soon introduce a new theme featuring Shasta s classic flavors in an unsweetened, zero-calorie, refreshing sparkling water concept.
69891_15_ITEM1_P21_S0	More than 100 years old, Faygo products are primarily distributed east of the Mississippi River and include numerous unique flavors including RedPop , Moon Mist , and Rock n Rye .
69891_15_ITEM1_P21_S1	We also produce and market Ritz soft drinks and seltzers, primarily in the southeastern U.S., distribute Big Shot in New Orleans and surrounding areas, and offer St. Nick s soft drinks during the holiday season.
69891_15_ITEM1_P21_S2	During recent years, we reformulated many of our brands to reduce the caloric content while still preserving their time-tested flavor profiles.
69891_15_ITEM1_P22_S0	Our Brands, optically and content-wise, are always a work in process.
69891_15_ITEM1_P22_S1	As often as innovation develops, we endeavor to significantly improve them, striving for quality and authenticity over cost.
69891_15_ITEM1_P23_S0	Our twelve manufacturing facilities are strategically located near major metropolitan markets across the continental United States.
69891_15_ITEM1_P23_S1	The locations of our plants enable us to efficiently manufacture and distribute beverages to substantially all geographic markets in the United States, including all of the top 25 metropolitan statistical areas.
69891_15_ITEM1_P23_S2	Each manufacturing facility is generally equipped to produce both canned and bottled beverage products in a variety of package sizes.
69891_15_ITEM1_P23_S3	We utilize numerous package types and sizes, including cans ranging from eight to sixteen ounces and bottles ranging from ten ounces to three liters.
69891_15_ITEM1_P24_S0	We believe that the innovative and controlled vertical integration of our bottling facilities provides an advantage over certain of our competitors that rely upon independent third party bottlers to manufacture and market their products.
69891_15_ITEM1_P24_S1	Since we control the national production, distribution and marketing of our brands, we believe we can more effectively manage product quality and customer service and respond quickly to changing market conditions.
69891_15_ITEM1_P25_S0	We produce a substantial portion of the flavor concentrates used in our branded products.
69891_15_ITEM1_P25_S1	By controlling our own formulas throughout our bottling network, we can manufacture our products in accordance with uniform quality standards while tailoring flavors to regional taste preferences.
69891_15_ITEM1_P25_S2	We believe that the combination of a Company-owned bottling network, together with uniform standards for packaging, formulations and customer service, provides us with a strategic advantage in servicing national retailers and mass-merchandisers.
69891_15_ITEM1_P25_S3	We also maintain research and development laboratories at multiple locations.
69891_15_ITEM1_P25_S4	These laboratories continually test products for compliance with our strict quality control standards as well as conduct research for new products and flavors.
69891_15_ITEM1_P26_S0	We utilize a hybrid distribution system to deliver our products through three primary distribution channels: take-home, convenience and food-service.
69891_15_ITEM1_P27_S0	The take-home distribution channel consists of national and regional grocery stores, warehouse clubs, mass-merchandisers, wholesalers and dollar stores.
69891_15_ITEM1_P27_S1	We distribute our products to this channel through the warehouse distribution system and the direct-store delivery system.
69891_15_ITEM1_P28_S0	Under the warehouse distribution system, products are shipped from our manufacturing facilities to the retailer s centralized distribution centers and then distributed by the retailer to each of its outlet locations with other goods.
69891_15_ITEM1_P28_S1	Products sold through the direct-store delivery system are distributed directly to the customer s retail outlets by our direct-store delivery fleet and by independent distributors.
69891_15_ITEM1_P29_S0	We distribute our products to the convenience channel through our own direct-store delivery fleet and those of independent distributors.
69891_15_ITEM1_P30_S0	The convenience channel consists of convenience stores, gas stations and other smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts.
69891_15_ITEM1_P30_S1	Because of the higher retail prices and margins that typically prevail, we have undertaken several measures to expand convenience channel distribution.
69891_15_ITEM1_P30_S2	These include development of products, packaging and graphics specifically targeted to this market.
69891_15_ITEM1_P31_S0	Our food-service division distributes products to independent, specialized distributors who sell to hospitals, schools, military bases, airlines, hotels and food-service wholesalers.
69891_15_ITEM1_P31_S1	Also, our Company-owned direct-store delivery fleet distributes products to certain schools and other food-service customers.
69891_15_ITEM1_P32_S0	Our take-home, convenience and food-service operations use vending machines and glass-door coolers as marketing and promotional tools for our brands.
69891_15_ITEM1_P32_S1	We provide vending machines and coolers on a placement or purchase basis to our customers.
69891_15_ITEM1_P32_S2	We believe vending and cooler equipment increases beverage sales, enhances brand awareness and develops brand loyalty.
69891_15_ITEM1_P33_S0	We sell and market our products through an internal sales force as well as specialized broker networks.
69891_15_ITEM1_P33_S1	Our sales force is organized to serve a specific market, focusing on one or more geographic territories, distribution channels or product lines.
69891_15_ITEM1_P33_S2	We believe this focus allows our sales group to provide high level, responsive service and support to our customers and markets.
69891_15_ITEM1_P34_S0	The emphasis of our sales and marketing programs is to maintain and enhance consumer brand recognition and loyalty, typically through a combination of regional advertising, special event marketing, endorsements, sponsorships and social media, along with consumer coupon distribution and product sampling.
69891_15_ITEM1_P34_S1	We retain advertising agencies to assist with media advertising programs for our brands.
69891_15_ITEM1_P34_S2	Additionally, we offer numerous promotional programs to retail customers, including cooperative advertising support, in-store advertising materials and other incentives.
69891_15_ITEM1_P34_S3	These elements allow us to tailor our marketing and advertising programs to meet local and regional economic conditions and demographics.
69891_15_ITEM1_P34_S4	Additionally, we sponsor special holiday promotions which feature St. Nick s soft drink and special holiday flavors and packaging.
69891_15_ITEM1_P35_S0	Our centralized procurement group maintains relationships with numerous suppliers of raw materials and packaging goods.
69891_15_ITEM1_P35_S1	By consolidating the purchasing function for our manufacturing facilities, we believe we are able to procure more competitive arrangements with our suppliers, thereby enhancing our ability to compete as a low-cost producer of beverages.
69891_15_ITEM1_P36_S0	The products we produce and sell are made from various materials including sweeteners, juice concentrates, carbon dioxide, water, glass and plastic bottles, aluminum cans and ends, paper, cartons and closures.
69891_15_ITEM1_P36_S1	Most of our low-calorie soft drink products use sucralose, aspartame, stevia or acesulfame potassium.
69891_15_ITEM1_P36_S2	We manufacture a substantial portion of our flavor concentrates and purchase remaining raw materials from multiple suppliers.
69891_15_ITEM1_P37_S0	Substantially all of the materials and ingredients we purchase are presently available from several suppliers, although strikes, weather conditions, utility shortages, governmental control or regulations, national emergencies, quality, price or supply fluctuations or other events outside our control could adversely affect the supply of specific materials.
69891_15_ITEM1_P37_S1	A significant portion of our raw material purchases, including aluminum cans, plastic bottles, high fructose corn syrup, corrugated packaging and juice concentrates, are derived from commodities.
69891_15_ITEM1_P37_S2	Therefore, pricing and availability tend to fluctuate based upon worldwide commodity market conditions.
69891_15_ITEM1_P37_S3	Our ability to recover increased costs through higher pricing may be limited by the competitive environment in which we operate.
69891_15_ITEM1_P37_S4	In certain cases, we may elect to enter into multi-year agreements for the supply of these materials with one or more suppliers, the terms of which may include variable or fixed pricing, minimum purchase quantities and/or the requirement to purchase all supplies for specified locations.
69891_15_ITEM1_P37_S5	Additionally, we use derivative financial instruments to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in certain raw material costs.
69891_15_ITEM1_P38_S0	The majority of our sales are seasonal with the highest volume typically realized during the summer months.
69891_15_ITEM1_P38_S1	We have sufficient production capacity to meet seasonal increases without maintaining significant quantities of inventory in anticipation of periods of peak demand.
69891_15_ITEM1_P38_S2	Additionally, our sales can be influenced by weather conditions.
69891_15_ITEM1_P39_S0	The beverage industry is highly competitive and our competitive position varies in each of our market areas.
69891_15_ITEM1_P39_S1	Our products compete with many varieties of liquid refreshment, including soft drinks, water products, juices, fruit drinks, powdered drinks, coffees, teas, energy drinks, sports drinks, dairy-based drinks, functional beverages and various other nonalcoholic beverages.
69891_15_ITEM1_P39_S2	We compete with bottlers and distributors of national, regional and private label products.
69891_15_ITEM1_P39_S3	Several competitors, including the two that dominate the soft drink industry, PepsiCo and The Coca-Cola Company, have greater financial resources than we have and aggressive promotion of their products can adversely affect sales of our brands.
69891_15_ITEM1_P40_S0	Principal methods of competition in the beverage industry are price and promotional activity, advertising and marketing programs, point-of-sale merchandising, retail space management, customer service, product differentiation, packaging innovations and distribution methods.
69891_15_ITEM1_P40_S1	We believe our Company differentiates itself through a diversified product portfolio, strong regional brand recognition, innovative flavor variety, attractive packaging, efficient distribution methods, specialized advertising and, for some product lines, value pricing.
69891_15_ITEM1_P41_S0	We own numerous trademarks for our brands that are significant to our business.
69891_15_ITEM1_P41_S1	We intend to continue to maintain all registrations of our significant trademarks and use the trademarks in the operation of our businesses.
69891_15_ITEM1_P42_S0	The production, distribution and sale of our products in the United States are subject to the Federal Food, Drug and Cosmetic Act; the Dietary Supplement Health and Education Act of 1994; the Occupational Safety and Health Act; the Lanham Act; various environmental statutes; and various other federal, state and local statutes regulating the production, transportation, sale, safety, advertising, labeling and ingredients of such products.
69891_15_ITEM1_P42_S1	We believe that we are in compliance, in all material respects, with such existing legislation.

69891_15_ITEM1_P43_S1	These requirements vary by each jurisdiction.

69891_15_ITEM1_P43_S3	We are unable to predict whether such legislation will be enacted or what impact its enactment would have on our business, financial condition or results of operations.

69891_15_ITEM1_P44_S1	Compliance with these provisions has not had any material adverse effect on our financial or competitive position.

69891_15_ITEM1A_P0_S0	In addition to other information in this Annual Report on Form 10-K, the following risk factors should be considered carefully in evaluating the Company s business.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P0_S1	Our business, financial condition and results of operations could be materially and adversely affected by any of these risks.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P0_S2	Additional risks and uncertainties, including risks and uncertainties not presently known to the Company, or that the Company currently deems immaterial, may also impair our business and results of operations.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P1_S0	Changes in consumer preferences and taste.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P1_S1	There has been an increasing focus on health and wellness by beverage consumers, which may reduce demand for caloric carbonated soft drinks and increase the consumption of products perceived to deliver health, wellness and/or functionality.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P2_S0	If we do not adequately anticipate and react to changing demographics, consumer trends, health concerns and product preferences, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P3_S0	The beverage industry is extremely competitive.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P3_S1	Our products compete with a broad range of beverage products, most of which are manufactured and distributed by companies with substantially greater financial, marketing and distribution resources.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P3_S2	In order to generate future revenues and profits, we must continue to sell products that appeal to our customers and consumers.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P3_S3	Discounting and other actions by our competitors may make it more difficult to sustain revenues and profits.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P4_S0	Our retail customer base has been consolidating over the last several years resulting in fewer customers with increased purchasing power.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P4_S1	This increased purchasing power can limit our ability to increase pricing for our products with certain of our customers.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P4_S2	Our inability to meet the demands of our larger customers could lead to a loss of business and adversely affect our financial results.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P5_S0	The production of our products is dependent on certain raw materials, including aluminum, resin, corn, linerboard, water and fruit juice.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P5_S1	In addition, the production and distribution of our products is dependent on energy sources, including natural gas, fuel and electricity.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P5_S2	These items are subject to price volatility caused by numerous factors.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P5_S3	Commodity price increases ultimately result in a corresponding increase in the cost of raw materials and energy.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P5_S4	We may be limited in our ability to pass these increases on to our customers or may incur a loss in sales volume to the extent price increases are taken.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P5_S5	In addition, strikes, weather conditions, governmental controls, national emergencies, natural disasters, supply shortages or other events could affect our continued supply of raw materials and energy.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P5_S6	If raw materials or energy costs increase, or the availability is limited, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P6_S0	Our business and properties are subject to various federal, state and local laws and regulations, including those governing the production, packaging, quality, labeling and distribution of beverage products.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P6_S1	In addition, various governmental agencies have considered limiting the consumption of and imposing additional taxes on soft drinks and other sweetened beverages, including those sweetened with high fructose corn syrup.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P6_S2	Changes in existing laws or regulations could negatively affect our financial results through lower sales or higher costs.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P7_S0	Sustained increases in the cost of employee benefits.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P7_S1	Our profitability is affected by the cost of medical and retirement benefits provided to employees.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P7_S2	In recent years, we have experienced significant increases in these costs as a result of certain factors beyond our control.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P7_S3	Although we seek to limit these cost increases, continued upward pressure in these costs could reduce our profitability.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P8_S0	Unfavorable weather conditions could have an adverse impact on our revenue and profitability.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P8_S1	Unusually cold or rainy weather may temporarily reduce demand for our products and contribute to lower sales, which could adversely affect our profitability for such periods.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P8_S2	Prolonged drought conditions in the geographic regions in which we do business could lead to restrictions on the use of water, which could adversely affect our ability to manufacture and distribute products.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P9_S0	We are dependent on key personnel .
69891_15_ITEM1A_P9_S1	Our performance significantly depends upon the continued contributions of our executive officers and key employees, both individually and as a group, and our ability to retain and motivate them.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P9_S2	Our officers and key personnel have many years of experience with us and in our industry and it may be difficult to replace them.
69891_15_ITEM1A_P9_S3	If we lose key personnel or are unable to recruit qualified personnel, our operations and ability to manage our business may be adversely affected.

69891_15_ITEM2_P0_S2	Two manufacturing facilities, located in Maryland and Florida, are leased subject to agreements that expire through 2020.
69891_15_ITEM2_P0_S3	We believe our facilities are generally in good condition and sufficient to meet our present needs.
69891_15_ITEM2_P1_S0	The production of beverages is capital intensive but is not characterized by rapid technological change.
69891_15_ITEM2_P1_S1	The technological advances that have occurred have generally been of an incremental cost-saving nature, such as the industry s conversion to lighter weight containers or improved blending processes that enhance ingredient yields.
69891_15_ITEM2_P1_S2	We are not aware of any anticipated industry-wide changes in technology that would adversely impact our current physical production capacity or cost of production.

69891_15_ITEM7_P0_S0	National Beverage Corp. is an acknowledged leader in the development, manufacturing, marketing and sale of a diverse portfolio of flavored beverage products.
69891_15_ITEM7_P0_S1	Our primary market focus is the United States, but our products are also distributed in Canada, Mexico, the Caribbean, Latin America, the Pacific Rim, Asia and Europe.
69891_15_ITEM7_P1_S0	A holding company for various operating subsidiaries, National Beverage Corp. was incorporated in Delaware in 1985 and began trading as a public company on the NASDAQ Stock Market in 1991.
69891_15_ITEM7_P1_S1	In this report, the terms we, us, our, Company and National Beverage mean National Beverage Corp. and its subsidiaries unless indicated otherwise.
69891_15_ITEM7_P2_S0	Our brands consist of (i) beverages geared toward the active and health-conscious consumer ( Power+ Brands ), including sparkling waters, energy drinks and shots, juices, and enhanced beverages, and (ii) Carbonated Soft Drinks in a variety of flavors including regular, sugar-free and reduced-calorie options.
69891_15_ITEM7_P2_S1	In addition, we produce soft drinks for certain retailers ( Allied Brands ) that endorse the Strategic Alliance concept of having our brands and Allied Brands marketed to effectuate enhanced growth of both.
69891_15_ITEM7_P3_S0	We employ a philosophy that emphasizes vertical integration; our manufacturing model integrates the procurement of raw materials and production of concentrates with the manufacture of finished products in our twelve manufacturing facilities.
69891_15_ITEM7_P3_S1	To service a diverse customer base that includes numerous national retailers as well as thousands of smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts, we have developed a hybrid distribution system that promotes and utilizes customer warehouse distribution facilities and our own direct-store delivery fleet plus the direct-store delivery systems of independent distributors and wholesalers.
69891_15_ITEM7_P4_S0	We consider ourselves to be a leader in the development and sale of flavored beverage products.
69891_15_ITEM7_P5_S0	The National Beverage Corp. brand portfolio contains a wide variety of beverages to meet consumer needs in a multitude of market segments.
69891_15_ITEM7_P5_S1	Our portfolio of Power+ Brands is targeted to consumers seeking healthier and functional alternatives to complement their active lifestyles, and includes LaCroix , LaCroix C rate and LaCroix NiCola sparkling water products; Rip It energy drinks and shots; and Everfresh and Everfresh Premier Varietals , 100% juice and juice-based products.
69891_15_ITEM7_P5_S2	Our carbonated soft drink flavor development spans more than 125 years originating with our flagship brands, Shasta and Faygo .
69891_15_ITEM7_P6_S0	Our strategy emphasizes the growth of our products by (i) expanding our focus on healthier and functional beverages tailored toward healthy, active lifestyles, (ii) offering a beverage portfolio of proprietary flavors with distinctive packaging and broad demographic appeal, (iii) supporting the franchise value of regional brands, (iv) appealing to the quality-value expectations of the family consumer, and (v) responding to demographic trends by developing innovative products designed to expand distribution.
69891_15_ITEM7_P7_S0	The majority of our sales are seasonal with the highest volume typically realized during the summer months.
69891_15_ITEM7_P7_S1	As a result, our operating results from one fiscal quarter to the next may not be comparable.
69891_15_ITEM7_P7_S2	Additionally, our operating results are affected by numerous factors, including fluctuations in the costs of raw materials, changes in consumer preference for beverage products, competitive pricing in the marketplace and weather conditions.
69891_15_ITEM7_P8_S0	increased .7% to $645.8 million as compared to $641.1 million for the fiscal year ended May 3, 2014 ( Fiscal 2014 ).
69891_15_ITEM7_P8_S1	The higher sales resulted from a 1.1% increase in case volume partially offset by a .4% decline in average selling price per unit.
69891_15_ITEM7_P8_S2	The increase in case volume reflects a 2.9% increase in branded volume, including a 15.3% case volume growth for our Power+ Brands, partially offset by a decline in Allied Brands.
69891_15_ITEM7_P9_S0	The decline in selling price per unit is related to changes in product mix.
69891_15_ITEM7_P10_S0	Net sales for the fiscal year ended May 3, 2014 decreased 3.2% to $641.1 million as compared to $662.0 million for the fiscal year ended April 27, 2013 ( Fiscal 2013 ).
69891_15_ITEM7_P10_S1	The lower sales resulted from a 7.5% volume decline in Carbonated Soft Drinks, principally due to extended periods of unfavorable weather conditions and industry-wide consumption decline.
69891_15_ITEM7_P10_S2	This volume decline was partially offset by case volume growth of 8.2% for our Power+ Brands.
69891_15_ITEM7_P10_S3	Average net selling price per case was approximately the same for both years.
69891_15_ITEM7_P11_S0	Gross Profit Gross profit approximated 33.9% of net sales for Fiscal 2015 and Fiscal 2014.
69891_15_ITEM7_P11_S1	Cost of sales per unit declined .3% primarily due to product mix changes.
69891_15_ITEM7_P12_S0	Gross profit was 33.9% of net sales for Fiscal 2014, which represents a 1.1% margin improvement compared to Fiscal 2013.
69891_15_ITEM7_P12_S1	The gross margin improvement is primarily due to favorable product mix changes and lower raw material costs.
69891_15_ITEM7_P12_S2	Cost of sales decreased 1.7% on a per case basis.
69891_15_ITEM7_P13_S0	Shipping and handling costs are included in selling, general and administrative expenses, the classification of which is consistent with many beverage companies.
69891_15_ITEM7_P13_S1	However, our gross margin may not be comparable to companies that include shipping and handling costs in cost of sales.

69891_15_ITEM7_P14_S1	Fiscal 2015 expenses reflect lower selling and marketing costs.
69891_15_ITEM7_P15_S0	Selling, general and administrative expenses were $153.2 million or 23.9% of net sales for Fiscal 2014 compared to $146.2 million or 22.1% of net sales for Fiscal 2013.
69891_15_ITEM7_P15_S1	Fiscal 2014 expenses reflect higher selling and marketing costs, primarily due to increased advertising expenses.

69891_15_ITEM7_P34_S0	Credit Risk We sell products to a variety of customers and extend credit based on an evaluation of each customer s financial condition, generally without requiring collateral.
69891_15_ITEM7_P34_S1	Exposure to credit losses varies by customer principally due to the financial condition of each customer.
69891_15_ITEM7_P34_S2	We monitor our exposure to credit losses and maintain allowances for anticipated losses based on specific customer circumstances, credit conditions and historical write-offs.
69891_15_ITEM7_P35_S0	Impairment of Long-Lived Assets All long-lived assets, excluding goodwill and intangible assets not subject to amortization, are evaluated for impairment on the basis of undiscounted cash flows whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable.
69891_15_ITEM7_P35_S1	An impaired asset is written down to its estimated fair market value based on the best information available.
69891_15_ITEM7_P36_S0	Estimated fair market value is generally measured by discounting future cash flows.
69891_15_ITEM7_P37_S0	Goodwill and intangible assets not subject to amortization are evaluated for impairment annually or sooner if we believe such assets may be impaired.
69891_15_ITEM7_P37_S1	An impairment loss is recognized if the carrying amount or, for goodwill, the carrying amount of its reporting unit, is greater than its fair value.
69891_15_ITEM7_P38_S0	Income Taxes Our effective income tax rate is based on estimates of taxes which will ultimately be payable.
69891_15_ITEM7_P38_S1	Deferred taxes are recorded to give recognition to temporary differences between the tax bases of assets or liabilities and their reported amounts in the financial statements.
69891_15_ITEM7_P38_S2	Valuation allowances are established to reduce the carrying amounts of deferred tax assets when it is deemed, more likely than not, that the benefit of deferred tax assets will not be realized.
69891_15_ITEM7_P39_S0	Insurance Programs We maintain self-insured and deductible programs for certain liability, medical and workers compensation exposures.
69891_15_ITEM7_P39_S1	Accordingly, we accrue for known claims and estimated incurred but not reported claims not otherwise covered by insurance based on actuarial assumptions and historical claims experience.
69891_15_ITEM7_P40_S0	We offer various sales incentive arrangements to our customers that require customer performance or achievement of certain sales volume targets.
69891_15_ITEM7_P40_S1	When the incentive is paid in advance, we amortize the amount paid over the period of benefit or contractual sales volume; otherwise, we accrue the expected amount to be paid over the period of benefit or expected sales volume.
69891_15_ITEM7_P40_S2	The recognition of these incentives involves the use of judgment related to performance and sales volume estimates that are made based on historical experience and other factors.
69891_15_ITEM7_P40_S3	Sales incentives are accounted for as a reduction of sales and actual amounts ultimately realized may vary from accrued amounts.

69891_15_ITEM7A_P0_S0	Commodities We purchase various raw materials, including aluminum cans, plastic bottles, high fructose corn syrup, corrugated packaging and juice concentrates, the prices of which fluctuate based on commodity market conditions.
69891_15_ITEM7A_P0_S1	Our ability to recover increased costs through higher pricing may be limited by the competitive environment in which we operate.
69891_15_ITEM7A_P0_S2	At times, we manage our exposure to this risk through the use of supplier pricing agreements that enable us to establish the purchase prices for certain commodities.
69891_15_ITEM7A_P0_S3	Additionally, we use derivative financial instruments to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in certain raw material costs.

69891_15_ITEM8_P16_S2	At May 2, 2015 and May 3, 2014, other liabilities included accruals of $5.9 million and $6.1 million, respectively, for estimated non-current risk retention exposures, of which $4.7 million and $5.1 million were covered by insurance.
69891_15_ITEM8_P17_S0	Intangible Assets Intangible assets as of May 2, 2015 and May 3, 2014 consisted of non-amortizable trademarks.
69891_15_ITEM8_P18_S0	Inventories Inventories are stated at the lower of first-in, first-out cost or market.
69891_15_ITEM8_P18_S1	Inventories at May 2, 2015 were comprised of finished goods of $24.9 million and raw materials of $18.0 million.
69891_15_ITEM8_P18_S2	Inventories at May 3, 2014 were comprised of finished goods of $27.2 million and raw materials of $16.7 million.
69891_15_ITEM8_P19_S0	Marketing Costs We are involved in a variety of marketing programs, including cooperative advertising programs with customers, to advertise and promote our products to consumers.
69891_15_ITEM8_P19_S1	Marketing costs are expensed when incurred, except for prepaid advertising and production costs which are expensed when the advertising takes place.
69891_15_ITEM8_P19_S2	Marketing costs, which are included in selling, general and administrative expenses, totaled $42.4 million in Fiscal 2015, $50.2 million in Fiscal 2014 and $44.6 million in Fiscal 2013.
69891_15_ITEM8_P20_S0	In May 2014, the FASB issued Accounting Standards Update No. 2014-09, Revenue from Contracts with Customers (Topic 606) ( ASU 2014-09 ).
69891_15_ITEM8_P20_S1	ASU 2014-09 requires an entity to recognize revenue in an amount that reflects the consideration to which the entity expects to receive in exchange for goods or services.
69891_15_ITEM8_P20_S2	ASU 2014-09 is effective for our fiscal year beginning April 30, 2017.
69891_15_ITEM8_P20_S3	We are currently evaluating the potential impact of adopting this guidance on our consolidated financial statements.
69891_15_ITEM8_P21_S0	Property, Plant and Equipment Property, plant and equipment are recorded at cost.
69891_15_ITEM8_P21_S1	Additions, replacements and betterments are capitalized, while maintenance and repairs that do not extend the useful life of an asset are expensed as incurred.
69891_15_ITEM8_P21_S2	Depreciation is recorded using the straight-line method over estimated useful lives of 7 to 30 years for buildings and improvements and 3 to 15 years for machinery and equipment.
69891_15_ITEM8_P21_S3	Leasehold improvements are amortized using the straight-line method over the shorter of the remaining lease term or the estimated useful life of the improvement.
69891_15_ITEM8_P22_S0	When assets are retired or otherwise disposed, the cost and accumulated depreciation are removed from the respective accounts and any related gain or loss is recognized.
69891_15_ITEM8_P23_S0	Revenue Recognition Revenue from product sales is recognized when title and risk of loss pass to the customer, which generally occurs upon delivery.
69891_15_ITEM8_P24_S0	Our policy is not to allow the return of products once they have been accepted by the customer.
69891_15_ITEM8_P24_S1	However, on occasion, we have accepted returns or issued credit to customers, primarily for damaged goods.
69891_15_ITEM8_P24_S2	The amounts have been immaterial and, accordingly, we do not provide a specific valuation allowance for sales returns.
69891_15_ITEM8_P25_S0	We offer various sales incentive arrangements to our customers that require customer performance or achievement of certain sales volume targets.
69891_15_ITEM8_P25_S1	When the incentive is paid in advance, we amortize the amount paid over the period of benefit or contractual sales volume; otherwise, we accrue the expected amount to be paid over the period of benefit or expected sales volume.
69891_15_ITEM8_P25_S2	The recognition of these incentives involves the use of judgment related to performance and sales volume estimates that are made based on historical experience and other factors.
69891_15_ITEM8_P25_S3	Sales incentives are accounted for as a reduction of sales and actual amounts ultimately realized may vary from accrued amounts.
69891_15_ITEM8_P26_S0	We operate as a single operating segment for purposes of presenting financial information and evaluating performance.
69891_15_ITEM8_P26_S1	As such, the accompanying consolidated financial statements present financial information in a format that is consistent with the internal financial information used by management.
69891_15_ITEM8_P26_S2	We do not accumulate revenues by product classification and, therefore, it is impractical to present such information.
69891_15_ITEM8_P27_S0	Shipping and Handling Costs Shipping and handling costs are reported in selling, general and administrative expenses in the accompanying consolidated statements of income.
69891_15_ITEM8_P27_S1	Such costs aggregated $44.4 million in Fiscal 2015 and Fiscal 2014 and $44.2 million in Fiscal 2013.
69891_15_ITEM8_P28_S0	Although our classification is consistent with many beverage companies, our gross margin may not be comparable to companies that include shipping and handling costs in cost of sales.
69891_15_ITEM8_P29_S0	Stock-Based Compensation Compensation expense for stock-based compensation awards is recognized over the vesting period based on the grant-date fair value estimated using the Black-Scholes model.
69891_15_ITEM8_P30_S0	Trade Receivables We record trade receivables at net realizable value, which includes an appropriate allowance for doubtful accounts.
69891_15_ITEM8_P30_S1	We extend credit based on an evaluation of each customer s financial condition, generally without requiring collateral.
69891_15_ITEM8_P31_S0	Exposure to credit losses varies by customer principally due to the financial condition of each customer.
69891_15_ITEM8_P31_S1	We monitor our exposure to credit losses and maintain allowances for anticipated losses based on specific customer circumstances, credit conditions and historical write-offs.
69891_15_ITEM8_P31_S2	Activity in the allowance for doubtful accounts was as follows:
69891_15_ITEM8_P32_S0	As of May 2, 2015 and May 3, 2014, we did not have any customer that comprised more than 10% of trade receivables.
69891_15_ITEM8_P32_S1	No one customer accounted for more than 10% of net sales during any of the last three fiscal years.
69891_15_ITEM8_P33_S0	The preparation of financial statements in conformity with United States generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported in the financial statements and accompanying notes.
69891_15_ITEM8_P33_S1	Although these estimates are based on management s knowledge of current events and anticipated future actions, actual results may vary from reported amounts.

69891_15_ITEM8_P46_S0	The Company is a party to a management agreement with Corporate Management Advisors, Inc. ( CMA ), a corporation owned by our Chairman and Chief Executive Officer.
69891_15_ITEM8_P46_S1	This agreement was originated in 1991 for the efficient use of management of two public companies at the time.
69891_15_ITEM8_P46_S2	In 1994, one of those public entities, through a merger, no longer was managed in this manner.
69891_15_ITEM8_P47_S0	Under the terms of the agreement, CMA provides, subject to the direction and supervision of the Board of Directors of the Company, (i) senior corporate functions (including supervision of the Company s financial, legal, executive recruitment, internal audit and management information systems departments) as well as the services of a Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, and (ii) services in connection with acquisitions, dispositions and financings by the Company, including identifying and profiling acquisition candidates, negotiating and structuring potential transactions and arranging financing for any such transaction.
69891_15_ITEM8_P47_S1	CMA, through its personnel, also provides, to the extent possible, the stimulus and creativity to develop an innovative and dynamic persona for the Company, its products and corporate image.
69891_15_ITEM8_P48_S0	In order to fulfill its obligations under the management agreement, CMA employs numerous individuals, whom, acting as a unit, provide management, administrative and creative functions for the Company.
69891_15_ITEM8_P48_S1	The management agreement provides that the Company will pay CMA an annual base fee equal to one percent of the consolidated net sales of the Company, and further provides that the Compensation and Stock Option Committee and the Board of Directors may from time to time award additional incentive compensation to CMA.
69891_15_ITEM8_P48_S2	The Board of Directors on numerous occasions contemplated incentive compensation and, while shareholder value has increased over 2,000% since the inception of this agreement, no incentive compensation has been paid.
69891_15_ITEM8_P49_S0	We incurred management fees to CMA of $6.5 million for Fiscal 2015, $6.4 million for Fiscal 2014 and $6.6 million for Fiscal 2013.
69891_15_ITEM8_P49_S1	Included in accounts payable were amounts due CMA of $1.6 million at May 2, 2015 and at May 3, 2014.
69891_15_ITEM8_P50_S0	From time to time, we enter into aluminum swap contracts to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in the cost of aluminum cans.
69891_15_ITEM8_P50_S1	Such financial instruments are designated and accounted for as a cash flow hedge.
69891_15_ITEM8_P50_S2	Accordingly, gains or losses attributable to the effective portion of the cash flow hedge are reported in Accumulated Other Comprehensive Income (Loss) ( AOCI ) and reclassified into earnings through cost of sales in the period in which the hedged transaction affects earnings.
69891_15_ITEM8_P51_S0	The ineffective portion of the change in fair value of our cash flow hedge was immaterial.

69891_15_ITEM8_P66_S0	Our stock-based compensation program is a broad-based program designed to attract and retain employees while also aligning employees interests with the interests of the shareholders.
69891_15_ITEM8_P67_S0	The 1991 Omnibus Incentive Plan (the Omnibus Plan ) provides for compensatory awards consisting of (i) stock options or stock awards for up to 4,800,000 shares of common stock, (ii) stock appreciation rights, dividend equivalents, other stock-based awards in amounts up to 4,800,000 shares of common stock and (iii) performance awards consisting of any combination of the above.
69891_15_ITEM8_P67_S1	The Omnibus Plan is designed to provide an incentive to officers and certain other key employees and consultants by making available to them an opportunity to acquire a proprietary interest or to increase such interest in National Beverage.
69891_15_ITEM8_P68_S0	The number of shares or options which may be issued under stock-based awards to an individual is limited to 1,680,000 during any year.
69891_15_ITEM8_P68_S1	Awards may be granted for no cash consideration or such minimal cash consideration as may be required by law.
69891_15_ITEM8_P69_S0	Options generally have an exercise price equal to the fair market value of our common stock on the date of grant, vest over a five-year period and expire after ten years.
69891_15_ITEM8_P70_S0	The Special Stock Option Plan provides for the issuance of stock options to purchase up to an aggregate of 1,800,000 shares of common stock.
69891_15_ITEM8_P70_S1	Options may be granted for such consideration as determined by the Board of Directors.
69891_15_ITEM8_P70_S2	The vesting schedule and exercise price of these options are tied to the recipient s ownership level of common stock and the terms generally allow for the reduction in exercise price upon each vesting period.
69891_15_ITEM8_P70_S3	Also, the Board of Directors authorized the issuance of options to purchase up to 50,000 shares of common stock to be issued at the direction of the Chairman.
69891_15_ITEM8_P71_S0	The Key Employee Equity Partnership Program ( KEEP Program ) provides for the granting of stock options to purchase up to 240,000 shares of common stock to key employees, consultants, directors and officers.
69891_15_ITEM8_P71_S1	Participants who purchase shares of stock in the open market receive grants of stock options equal to 50% of the number of shares purchased, up to a maximum of 6,000 shares in any two-year period.
69891_15_ITEM8_P71_S2	Options under the KEEP Program are forfeited in the event of the sale of shares used to acquire such options.
69891_15_ITEM8_P71_S3	Options are granted at an initial exercise price of 60% of the purchase price paid for the shares acquired and the exercise price reduces to the stock par value at the end of the six-year vesting period.
69891_15_ITEM8_P72_S0	We account for stock options under the fair value method of accounting using a Black-Scholes valuation model to estimate the stock option fair value at date of grant.
69891_15_ITEM8_P72_S1	The fair value of stock options is amortized to expense over the vesting period.
69891_15_ITEM8_P72_S2	Stock options granted were 276,800 shares in Fiscal 2015, 5,245 shares in Fiscal 2014 and 2,000 shares in Fiscal 2013.
69891_15_ITEM8_P72_S3	The weighted average Black-Scholes fair value assumptions for stock options granted are as follows: weighted average expected life of 7.4 years for Fiscal 2015, 8 years for Fiscal 2014 and 8 years for Fiscal 2013; weighted average expected volatility of 32.8% for Fiscal 2015, 35.8% for Fiscal 2014 and 38.1% for Fiscal 2013; weighted average risk free interest rates of 2.2% for Fiscal 2015, 1.9% for Fiscal 2014 and 1.6% for Fiscal 2013; and expected dividend yield of 4.6% for Fiscal 2015, 4.6% for Fiscal 2014 and 5.0% for Fiscal 2013.
69891_15_ITEM8_P73_S0	The expected life of stock options was estimated based on historical experience.
69891_15_ITEM8_P73_S1	The expected volatility was estimated based on historical stock prices for a period consistent with the expected life of stock options.
69891_15_ITEM8_P73_S2	The risk free interest rate was based on the U.S. Treasury constant maturity interest rate whose term is consistent with the expected life of stock options.
69891_15_ITEM8_P73_S3	Forfeitures were estimated based on historical experience and ranged from 0% to 16% for Fiscal 2015, Fiscal 2014 and Fiscal 2013.

69891_15_ITEM8_P91_S0	To the Board of Directors and Shareholders of National Beverage Corp.
69891_15_ITEM8_P92_S0	We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of National Beverage Corp. as of May 2, 2015 and May 3, 2014 and the related consolidated statements of income, comprehensive income, shareholders equity and cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended May 2, 2015.
69891_15_ITEM8_P92_S1	We also have audited National Beverage Corp. s internal control over financial reporting as of May 2, 2015, based on criteria established in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO) in 2013.
69891_15_ITEM8_P92_S2	National Beverage Corp. s management is responsible for these financial statements, for maintaining effective internal control over financial reporting and for its assessment of the effectiveness of internal control over financial reporting included in the accompanying Management s Report on Internal Control over Financial Reporting.
69891_15_ITEM8_P92_S3	Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements and an opinion on the Company s internal control over financial reporting based on our audits.
69891_15_ITEM8_P93_S0	We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).
69891_15_ITEM8_P93_S1	Those standards require that we plan and perform the audits to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement and whether effective internal control over financial reporting was maintained in all material respects.
69891_15_ITEM8_P93_S2	Our audits of the financial statements included examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management and evaluating the overall financial statement presentation.
69891_15_ITEM8_P93_S3	Our audit of internal control over financial reporting included obtaining an understanding of internal control over financial reporting, assessing the risk that a material weakness exists and testing and evaluating the design and operating effectiveness of internal control based on the assessed risk.
69891_15_ITEM8_P93_S4	Our audits also included performing such other procedures as we considered necessary in the circumstances.
69891_15_ITEM8_P93_S5	We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinions.
69891_15_ITEM8_P94_S0	A company s internal control over financial reporting is a process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
69891_15_ITEM8_P94_S1	A company s internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that (1) pertain to the maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and dispositions of the assets of the company; (2) provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles and that receipts and expenditures of the company are being made only in accordance with authorizations of management and directors of the company; and (3) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use, or disposition of the company s assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
69891_15_ITEM8_P95_S0	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
69891_15_ITEM8_P95_S1	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
69891_15_ITEM8_P96_S0	In our opinion, the consolidated financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of National Beverage Corp. as of May 2, 2015 and May 3, 2014 and the results of their operations and their cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended May 2, 2015, in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.
69891_15_ITEM8_P96_S1	Also in our opinion, National Beverage Corp. maintained, in all material respects, effective internal control over financial reporting as of May 2, 2015, based on criteria established in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO) in 2013.
69891_15_ITEM9A_P0_S0	Disclosure Controls and Procedures As of the end of the period covered by this Annual Report on Form 10-K, we carried out an evaluation, under the supervision and with the participation of the Company s management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, of the effectiveness of the design and operation of our disclosure controls and procedures (as defined in Rule 13a-15(e) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the Exchange Act )).
69891_15_ITEM9A_P0_S1	Based upon that evaluation, the Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer concluded that our disclosure controls and procedures were effective to ensure information required to be disclosed by us in reports we file or submit under the Exchange Act is (1) recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified in SEC rules and forms and (2) accumulated and communicated to our management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, to allow timely decisions regarding required disclosure.
69891_15_ITEM9A_P1_S0	Our management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting, as such term is defined in Rule 13a-15(f) of the Exchange Act.
69891_15_ITEM9A_P1_S1	Under the supervision and with the participation of our management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, we conducted an evaluation of the effectiveness of our internal control over financial reporting based on the framework in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission in 2013.
69891_15_ITEM9A_P1_S2	Based on that evaluation, our management concluded that our internal control over financial reporting was effective as of May 2, 2015.
69891_15_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Management recognizes that there are inherent limitations in the effectiveness of any internal control over financial reporting, including the possibility of human error and the circumvention or overriding of internal control.
69891_15_ITEM9A_P2_S1	Accordingly, even effective internal control over financial reporting can provide only reasonable assurance with respect to financial statement preparation.
69891_15_ITEM9A_P2_S2	Further, because of changes in conditions, the effectiveness of internal control may vary over time.
