69891_16_ITEM1_P0_S0	National Beverage Corp. proudly refreshes America with a distinctive portfolio of Sparkling Waters, Juices, Energy Drinks and Carbonated Soft Drinks.
69891_16_ITEM1_P0_S1	We believe our ingenious product designs, innovative packaging and imaginative flavors, along with our corporate culture and philosophy, makes National Beverage unique in the beverage industry.
69891_16_ITEM1_P1_S0	The Company s primary market focus is the United States, but our products are also distributed in various other countries.
69891_16_ITEM1_P2_S0	National Beverage Corp. was incorporated in Delaware in 1985 and began trading as a public company on the NASDAQ Stock Market in 1991.
69891_16_ITEM1_P2_S1	In this report, the terms we, us, our, Company and National Beverage mean National Beverage Corp. and its subsidiaries unless indicated otherwise.
69891_16_ITEM1_P3_S0	National Beverage is in an ongoing transition to meet the healthy hydration demands of the American consumer.
69891_16_ITEM1_P3_S1	Health and wellness awareness has increased significantly, resulting in growing demand for beverages with little or no calories and wholesome natural ingredients.
69891_16_ITEM1_P4_S0	Our brands emphasize distinctly-flavored beverages in attractive packaging that appeal to multiple demographic groups.
69891_16_ITEM1_P4_S1	The attentive, conscious and discriminating consumer is ever more alert to healthy choices and better-for-you ingredients that align to this transition and strategic focus.
69891_16_ITEM1_P5_S0	We believe the combination of our business strategies and philosophies is key to greater competitive advantage and differentiation from competitors.
69891_16_ITEM1_P5_S1	Points of differentiation include the following:
69891_16_ITEM1_P6_S0	We focus on developing healthier beverages in response to the global shift in consumer buying habits.
69891_16_ITEM1_P6_S1	We are committed to tailoring the variety and types of beverages in our portfolio to satisfy the preferences of a diverse mix of crossover consumers a growing group desiring a change to better-for-you beverages.
69891_16_ITEM1_P7_S0	F lavor Innovation Throughout our product lines and brands, we emphasize distinctly flavored beverages.
69891_16_ITEM1_P7_S1	Building on a rich tradition of flavor and brand innovation with over a 125 year history of development with iconic brands such as Shasta and Faygo , we consider ourselves a leader in flavor and essence technology.
69891_16_ITEM1_P8_S0	Proprietary flavors and essences are developed and tested in-house and only made commercially available after extensive concept and sensory evaluation.
69891_16_ITEM1_P8_S1	Our variety of flavors provides us a unique advantage with today s consumers who demand variety and refreshing beverage alternatives.
69891_16_ITEM1_P9_S0	Quality Ethic We believe consumers demand quality, and we are committed to producing and developing products of the highest quality that also appeal to the value expectations of the consumer.
69891_16_ITEM1_P9_S1	We believe we can leverage our efficient production and distribution systems, and our cost-effective social media and regionally focused marketing programs, to profitably deliver products at optimal consumer price-points.
69891_16_ITEM1_P10_S0	Creative Dynamics In a beverage industry that is dominated by the cola giants , we pride ourselves on our ability to respond faster and more creatively to consumer trends than competitors who are burdened by production and distribution complexity as well as legacy costs.
69891_16_ITEM1_P10_S1	The ability to identify consumer trends and create new product concepts to lead the market defines our new product development model.
69891_16_ITEM1_P10_S2	Speed to market with the right concept, unique flavor creation and trend forward better-for-you continues to be our goal.
69891_16_ITEM1_P10_S3	As with flavor development, internal development teams are responsible for concept creation, packaging and design, which allows for rapid go to market timing and reduced development costs.
69891_16_ITEM1_P11_S0	Our brands consist of (i) beverages geared to the active and health-conscious consumer ( Power+ Brands ) including sparkling waters, energy drinks, and juices, and (ii) Carbonated Soft Drinks in a variety of flavors including regular, sugar-free and reduced calorie options.
69891_16_ITEM1_P11_S1	We believe our unique brands and speed-to-market are key factors to our success.
69891_16_ITEM1_P12_S0	La Croix 100% all natural LaCroix Sparkling Water, our strategically largest and fastest-growing brand, has set the pace in the Sparkling Water category that is rapidly becoming the alternative to traditional carbonated soda.
69891_16_ITEM1_P12_S1	With zero calories, zero sweeteners and zero sodium, the innocence of LaCroix has propelled it to the top-selling all natural domestic sparkling water.
69891_16_ITEM1_P13_S0	LaCroix has the support of national chains in multiple channels, including mass merchants, mainstream supermarkets and natural and specialty food retailers and has a flourishing social media presence.
69891_16_ITEM1_P14_S0	Flavored with natural fruit essence, LaCroix has expanded its core line with five new offerings - Coconut, Mango, Apricot, Passionfruit and Tangerine.
69891_16_ITEM1_P15_S0	LaCroix s dynamic theme LaCroix C rate ( Cure Yourself ) celebrates French sophistication with Spanish zest with three new bold flavors Mel n Pomelo (cantaloupe pink grapefruit), M re Pepino (blackberry cucumber) and Kiwi Sandia (kiwi watermelon).
69891_16_ITEM1_P15_S1	C rate naturally refreshes in tall 12 oz.
69891_16_ITEM1_P15_S2	Eloquent graphics, robust aroma, naturally essenced and premium-priced, C rate is a trendsetting addition to a brand that is the healthy alternative for trend-forward consumers.
69891_16_ITEM1_P16_S0	NiCola by LaCroix, an innovative sparkling water with the essence and flavor of cola, is innocent of calories, sodium, sweetener or any ingredient that the health-conscious consumer avoids.
69891_16_ITEM1_P16_S1	NiCola is designed for those cola and diet cola drinkers within the $79 billion U.S. carbonated soft drink market who are looking to crossover to a beverage that complements a healthier lifestyle.
69891_16_ITEM1_P17_S0	Additional LaCroix themes are in development and feature unique packaging, ground-breaking flavor concepts, and a go-to-market strategy designed to provide additional placements within the retail environment outside the traditional grocery shelf.
69891_16_ITEM1_P18_S0	Shasta Sparkling Shasta Sparkling Water duplicates the iconic flavors that have charmed its loyal consumers over the past 125 plus years with the first genuine soft-drink alternative (SDA).
69891_16_ITEM1_P19_S0	Shasta Sparkling is naturally-essenced without calories, sodium and sweeteners.
69891_16_ITEM1_P19_S1	Simply Natural and Smartly Healthy , Shasta Sparkling flavors include: Lemon-Lime Splash, Draft Root Beer, Shasta Cola, California Orange, Original Pure and Big Black Cherry.
69891_16_ITEM1_P20_S0	Shasta Sparkling was successfully test marketed in the Western U.S. in the fourth quarter of fiscal year 2016 and has been introduced within Shasta s demographic areas to give carbonated soft drink consumers who want their nostalgic Shasta flavors an entirely innocent and exciting alternative.
69891_16_ITEM1_P21_S0	Shasta Sparkling complements a healthier lifestyle with its eloquent design and is packaged in tall 10.5 oz.
69891_16_ITEM1_P21_S1	cans with an industry first clean label.
69891_16_ITEM1_P22_S0	Ever f resh and Mr. Pure Everfresh 100% juice and juice drinks are available in a variety of flavors, from such classics as Orange, Cranberry and flavored lemonades to exotics that include Premium Papaya and Pineapple Mango.
69891_16_ITEM1_P23_S0	Originating in the Midwest, the Everfresh signature package is a hot-filled, 16 oz. glass bottle primarily for single-serve consumption.
69891_16_ITEM1_P23_S1	Additional consumer - friendly packages range from 10 oz.
69891_16_ITEM1_P24_S0	Everfresh Premier Varietals , a unique theme from Everfresh, is positioned as a stand-alone brand for display in the produce section of supermarkets.
69891_16_ITEM1_P24_S1	Everfresh Premier Varietals is a premium line of 100% natural apple juice derived from a variety of apples specific to the taste of the varietal, such as Granny Smith, McIntosh, Honey Crisp, Golden Delicious, Fuji and Pink Lady.
69891_16_ITEM1_P24_S2	Premier Varietals are packaged in award-winning 12 oz.
69891_16_ITEM1_P24_S3	glass bottles with decorative tamper-evident neck seals.
69891_16_ITEM1_P25_S0	Mr. Pure juice drinks are marketed in a variety of flavors, from classics like Apple, Orange and Grapefruit to unique flavors such as Peach Watermelon, Grape Cranberry and Island Punch.
69891_16_ITEM1_P26_S0	Mr. Pure is distributed in the Midwest primarily in 16 oz.
69891_16_ITEM1_P26_S1	glass bottles designed for single-serve consumption.
69891_16_ITEM1_P27_S0	Rip It Rip It energy fuel is the flavor innovator in the growing energy category with unique flavors, including six that are sugar-free, bringing variety and value to the widening consumer base.
69891_16_ITEM1_P27_S1	Rip It Tribute themed energy is a successful military inspired addition to the lineup that now includes its latest offering, Tribute Cherry Lime.
69891_16_ITEM1_P27_S2	Building on the flavor tradition of original Rip It, a 2 oz. sugar free shot version in seven flavors is marketed through our distribution system in multiple displayable package configurations.
69891_16_ITEM1_P28_S0	More than 125 years old , Shasta is recognized as a bottling industry pioneer and innovator.
69891_16_ITEM1_P28_S1	Shasta features multiple flavors, including products targeted to the growing Hispanic and other ethnic markets, and continues to earn consumer loyalty by delivering value, convenience and such unique tastes as California Dreamin , Very Cherry Twist and Fiesta Punch.
69891_16_ITEM1_P29_S0	More than 100 years old, Faygo products are primarily distributed east of the Mississippi River and include numerous unique flavors including Red Pop , Moon Mist , and Rock n Rye .
69891_16_ITEM1_P29_S1	We also produce and market Ritz soft drinks and seltzers, primarily in the southeastern U.S., distribute Big Shot in New Orleans and surrounding areas, and offer St. Nick s soft drinks during the holiday season.
69891_16_ITEM1_P29_S2	During recent years, we reformulated many of our brands to reduce the caloric content while still preserving their time-tested flavor profiles.
69891_16_ITEM1_P30_S0	Although typical cola drinks account for approximately 48% of the soft drink industry s domestic grocery channel volume, colas account for less than 15% of our total volume.
69891_16_ITEM1_P30_S1	We tailor our marketing and promotion programs by locale; many of our carbonated soft drink brands enjoy a regional identification that fosters long-term consumer loyalty and make them less vulnerable to competitive substitution.
69891_16_ITEM1_P30_S2	In addition, products produced locally often generate more aggressive retailer-sponsored promotional activities and receive media exposure through community activities rather than costly national advertising.
69891_16_ITEM1_P31_S0	Our brands, optically and ingredient-wise, are always a work in process.
69891_16_ITEM1_P31_S1	We are continually striving to make all our soft drinks healthier beverages while still maintaining their iconic taste profiles.
69891_16_ITEM1_P31_S2	As often as innovation develops, we endeavor to significantly improve our products, always seeking quality and authenticity over cost.
69891_16_ITEM1_P32_S0	We employ a philosophy that emphasizes vertical integration; our production model integrates the procurement of raw materials and crafting of concentrates with the production of finished products.
69891_16_ITEM1_P32_S1	Our twelve strategically located production facilities are near major metropolitan markets across the continental United States.
69891_16_ITEM1_P32_S2	The locations of our facilities enable us to efficiently produce and distribute beverages to substantially all geographic markets in the United States, including the top 25 metropolitan statistical areas.
69891_16_ITEM1_P32_S3	Each facility is generally equipped to produce both canned and bottled beverage products in a variety of package sizes.
69891_16_ITEM1_P32_S4	We utilize numerous package types and sizes, including cans ranging from eight to sixteen ounces and bottles ranging from ten ounces to three liters.
69891_16_ITEM1_P33_S0	We believe that the innovative and controlled vertical integration of our bottling facilities provides an advantage over certain of our competitors that rely upon independent third party bottlers to manufacture and market their products.
69891_16_ITEM1_P33_S1	Since we control the national production, distribution and marketing of our brands, we believe we can more effectively manage product quality and customer service and respond quickly to changing market conditions.
69891_16_ITEM1_P34_S0	We produce a substantial portion of the flavor concentrates used in our branded products.
69891_16_ITEM1_P34_S1	By controlling our own formulas throughout our bottling network, we can craft our products in accordance with uniform quality standards while tailoring flavors to regional taste preferences.
69891_16_ITEM1_P34_S2	We believe that the combination of a Company-owned bottling network, together with uniform standards for packaging, formulations and customer service, provides us with a strategic advantage in servicing national retailers and mass-merchandisers.
69891_16_ITEM1_P34_S3	We also maintain research and development laboratories at multiple locations.
69891_16_ITEM1_P34_S4	These laboratories continually test products for compliance with our strict quality control standards as well as conduct research for new products and flavors.
69891_16_ITEM1_P35_S0	To service a diverse customer base that includes numerous national retailers, as well as thousands of smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts, we utilize a hybrid distribution system to deliver our products through three primary distribution channels: take-home, convenience and food-service.
69891_16_ITEM1_P36_S0	The take-home distribution channel consists of national and regional grocery stores, warehouse clubs, mass-merchandisers, wholesalers and dollar stores.
69891_16_ITEM1_P36_S1	We distribute our products to this channel through the warehouse distribution system and the direct-store delivery system.
69891_16_ITEM1_P37_S0	Under the warehouse distribution system, products are shipped from our production facilities to the retailer s centralized distribution centers and then distributed by the retailer to each of its outlet locations with other goods.
69891_16_ITEM1_P37_S1	Products sold through the direct-store delivery system are distributed directly to the customer s retail outlets by our direct-store delivery fleet and by independent distributors.
69891_16_ITEM1_P38_S0	We distribute our products to the convenience channel through our own direct-store delivery fleet and those of independent distributors.
69891_16_ITEM1_P39_S0	The convenience channel consists of convenience stores, gas stations and other smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts.
69891_16_ITEM1_P39_S1	Because of the higher retail prices and margins that typically prevail, we have undertaken several measures to expand convenience channel distribution.
69891_16_ITEM1_P39_S2	These include development of products, packaging and graphics specifically targeted to this market.
69891_16_ITEM1_P40_S0	Our food-service division distributes products to independent, specialized distributors who sell to hospitals, schools, military bases, airlines, hotels and food-service wholesalers.
69891_16_ITEM1_P40_S1	Also, our Company-owned direct-store delivery fleet distributes products to certain schools and other food-service customers.
69891_16_ITEM1_P41_S0	Our take-home, convenience and food-service operations use vending machines and glass-door coolers as marketing and promotional tools for our brands.
69891_16_ITEM1_P41_S1	We provide vending machines and coolers on a placement or purchase basis to our customers.
69891_16_ITEM1_P41_S2	We believe vending and cooler equipment increases beverage sales, enhances brand awareness and develops brand loyalty.
69891_16_ITEM1_P42_S0	We sell and market our products through an internal sales force as well as specialized broker networks.
69891_16_ITEM1_P42_S1	Our sales force is organized to serve a specific market, focusing on one or more geographic territories, distribution channels or product lines.
69891_16_ITEM1_P42_S2	We believe this focus allows our sales group to provide high level, responsive service and support to our customers and markets.
69891_16_ITEM1_P43_S0	The emphasis of our sales and marketing programs is to maintain and enhance consumer brand recognition and loyalty, typically through a combination of regional advertising, special event marketing, endorsements, sponsorships and social media, along with consumer coupon distribution and product sampling.
69891_16_ITEM1_P43_S1	We retain agencies to assist with social media engagement and advertising programs for our brands.
69891_16_ITEM1_P43_S2	Additionally, we offer numerous promotional programs to retail customers, including cooperative advertising support, in-store advertising materials and other incentives.
69891_16_ITEM1_P43_S3	These elements allow tailored marketing and advertising programs to meet local and regional economic conditions and demographics.
69891_16_ITEM1_P43_S4	Additionally, we sponsor special holiday promotions which feature St. Nick s soft drinks and special holiday flavors and packaging.
69891_16_ITEM1_P44_S0	In recent years, we ve expanded our programs to reach consumers directly through innovative digital marketing, social media engagement and content creation.
69891_16_ITEM1_P44_S1	We are focused on increasing our digital presence and capabilities to further enhance the consumer experience across our brands.
69891_16_ITEM1_P45_S0	Our centralized procurement group maintains relationships with numerous suppliers of raw materials and packaging goods.
69891_16_ITEM1_P45_S1	By consolidating the purchasing function for our production facilities, we believe we are able to procure more competitive arrangements with our suppliers, thereby enhancing our ability to compete as a low-cost producer of beverages.
69891_16_ITEM1_P46_S0	The products we produce and sell are made from various materials including sweeteners, juice and flavor concentrates, carbon dioxide, water, glass and plastic bottles, aluminum cans, paper, cartons and closures.
69891_16_ITEM1_P46_S1	Most of our low-calorie soft drink products use sucralose, aspartame, stevia or acesulfame potassium.
69891_16_ITEM1_P46_S2	We craft a substantial portion of our flavor concentrates and purchase remaining raw materials from multiple suppliers.
69891_16_ITEM1_P47_S0	Substantially all of the materials and ingredients we purchase are presently available from several suppliers, although strikes, weather conditions, utility shortages, governmental control or regulations, national emergencies, quality, price or supply fluctuations or other events outside our control could adversely affect the supply of specific materials.
69891_16_ITEM1_P47_S1	A significant portion of our raw material purchases, including aluminum cans, plastic bottles, high fructose corn syrup, corrugated packaging and juice concentrates, are derived from commodities.
69891_16_ITEM1_P47_S2	Therefore, pricing and availability tend to fluctuate based upon worldwide commodity market conditions.
69891_16_ITEM1_P47_S3	Our ability to recover increased costs through higher pricing may be limited by the competitive environment in which we operate.
69891_16_ITEM1_P47_S4	In certain cases, we may elect to enter into multi-year agreements for the supply of these materials with one or more suppliers, the terms of which may include variable or fixed pricing, minimum purchase quantities and/or the requirement to purchase all supplies for specified locations.
69891_16_ITEM1_P47_S5	Additionally, we use derivative financial instruments to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in certain raw material costs.
69891_16_ITEM1_P48_S0	The majority of our sales are seasonal with the highest volume typically realized during the summer and warmer months.
69891_16_ITEM1_P48_S1	Additionally, our sales can be influenced by weather conditions.
69891_16_ITEM1_P49_S0	The beverage industry is highly competitive and our competitive position varies in each of our market areas.
69891_16_ITEM1_P49_S1	Our products compete with many varieties of liquid refreshment, including soft drinks, water products, juices, fruit drinks, powdered drinks, coffees, teas, energy drinks, sports drinks, dairy-based drinks, functional beverages and various other nonalcoholic beverages.
69891_16_ITEM1_P49_S2	We compete with bottlers and distributors of national, regional and private label products.
69891_16_ITEM1_P49_S3	Several competitors, including the two that dominate the soft drink industry, PepsiCo and The Coca-Cola Company, have greater financial resources than we have and aggressive promotion of their products can adversely affect sales of our brands.
69891_16_ITEM1_P50_S0	Principal methods of competition in the beverage industry are price and promotional activity, advertising and marketing programs, point-of-sale merchandising, retail space management, customer service, product differentiation, packaging innovations and distribution methods.
69891_16_ITEM1_P50_S1	We believe our Company differentiates itself through a diversified product portfolio, strong brand recognition, innovative flavor variety, attractive packaging, efficient distribution methods, focused advertising and social media, and, for some product lines, value pricing.
69891_16_ITEM1_P51_S0	We own numerous trademarks for our brands that are significant to our business.
69891_16_ITEM1_P51_S1	We intend to continue to maintain all registrations of our significant trademarks and use the trademarks in the operation of our businesses.
69891_16_ITEM1_P52_S0	The production, distribution and sale of our products in the United States are subject to the Federal Food, Drug and Cosmetic Act; the Dietary Supplement Health and Education Act of 1994; the Occupational Safety and Health Act; the Lanham Act; various environmental statutes; and various other federal, state and local statutes regulating the production, transportation, sale, safety, advertising, labeling and ingredients of such products.
69891_16_ITEM1_P52_S1	We believe that we are in compliance, in all material respects, with such existing legislation.
69891_16_ITEM1_P53_S0	Certain states and localities require a deposit or tax on the sale of certain beverages.
69891_16_ITEM1_P53_S1	These requirements vary by each jurisdiction.
69891_16_ITEM1_P53_S2	Similar legislation has been proposed in certain other states and localities, as well as by Congress.
69891_16_ITEM1_P53_S3	We are unable to predict whether such legislation will be enacted or what impact its enactment would have on our business, financial condition or results of operations.
69891_16_ITEM1_P54_S0	All of our facilities in the United States are subject to federal, state and local environmental laws and regulations.
69891_16_ITEM1_P54_S1	Compliance with these provisions has not had any material adverse effect on our financial or competitive position.
69891_16_ITEM1_P54_S2	We believe that our current practices and procedures for the control and disposition of toxic or hazardous substances comply in all material respects with applicable law.
69891_16_ITEM1_P54_S3	Compliance with or violation of any current or future regulations and legislation could require material expenditures or have a material adverse effect on our financial results.
69891_16_ITEM1_P55_S0	As of April 30, 2016, we employed approximately 1,200 people, of which approximately 300 are covered by collective bargaining agreements.
69891_16_ITEM1_P55_S1	We believe that relations with our employees are generally good.

69891_16_ITEM1A_P0_S0	In addition to other information in this Annual Report on Form 10-K, the following risk factors should be considered carefully in evaluating the Company s business.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P0_S1	Our business, financial condition and results of operations could be materially and adversely affected by any of these risks.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P0_S2	Additional risks and uncertainties, including risks and uncertainties not presently known to the Company, or that the Company currently deems immaterial, may also impair our business and results of operations.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P1_S0	Changes in consumer preferences and taste.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P1_S1	There has been an increasing focus on health and wellness by beverage consumers, which may reduce demand for caloric carbonated soft drinks and increase the consumption of products perceived to deliver health, wellness and/or functionality.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P2_S0	If we do not adequately anticipate and react to changing demographics, consumer trends, health concerns and product preferences, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P3_S0	The beverage industry is extremely competitive.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P3_S1	Our products compete with a broad range of beverage products, most of which are manufactured and distributed by companies with substantially greater financial, marketing and distribution resources.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P3_S2	In order to generate future revenues and profits, we must continue to sell products that appeal to our customers and consumers.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P3_S3	Discounting and other actions by our competitors may make it more difficult to sustain revenues and profits.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P4_S0	Our retail customer base has been consolidating over the last several years resulting in fewer customers with increased purchasing power.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P4_S1	This increased purchasing power can limit our ability to increase pricing for our products with certain of our customers.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P4_S2	Our inability to meet the demands of our larger customers could lead to a loss of business and adversely affect our financial results.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P5_S0	The production of our products is dependent on certain raw materials, including aluminum, resin, corn, linerboard, water and fruit juice.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P5_S1	In addition, the production and distribution of our products is dependent on energy sources, including natural gas, fuel and electricity.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P5_S2	These items are subject to price volatility caused by numerous factors.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P5_S3	Commodity price increases ultimately result in a corresponding increase in the cost of raw materials and energy.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P5_S4	We may be limited in our ability to pass these increases on to our customers or may incur a loss in sales volume to the extent price increases are taken.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P5_S5	In addition, strikes, weather conditions, governmental controls, national emergencies, natural disasters, supply shortages or other events could affect our continued supply of raw materials and energy.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P5_S6	If raw materials or energy costs increase, or the availability is limited, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P6_S0	Our business and properties are subject to various federal, state and local laws and regulations, including those governing the production, packaging, quality, labeling and distribution of beverage products.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P6_S1	In addition, various governmental agencies have enacted or considered imposing additional taxes on soft drinks and other sweetened beverages.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P6_S2	Changes in existing laws or regulations could negatively affect our financial results through lower sales or higher costs.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P7_S0	Sustained increases in the cost of employee benefits.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P7_S1	Our profitability is affected by the cost of medical and retirement benefits provided to employees, including employees covered under collective bargaining agreements and multi-employer pension plans.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P7_S2	In recent years, we have experienced increases in these costs as a result of certain factors beyond our control.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P7_S3	Although we seek to limit these cost increases, continued upward pressure in these costs could reduce our profitability.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P8_S0	Unfavorable weather conditions could have an adverse impact on our revenue and profitability.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P8_S1	Unusually cold or rainy weather may temporarily reduce demand for our products and contribute to lower sales, which could adversely affect our profitability for such periods.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P8_S2	Prolonged drought conditions in the geographic regions in which we do business could lead to restrictions on the use of water, which could adversely affect our ability to produce and distribute products.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P9_S0	Our performance significantly depends upon the continued contributions of our executive officers and key employees, both individually and as a group, and our ability to retain and motivate them.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P9_S1	Our officers and key personnel have many years of experience with us and in our industry and it may be difficult to replace them.
69891_16_ITEM1A_P9_S2	If we lose key personnel or are unable to recruit qualified personnel, our operations and ability to manage our business may be adversely affected.
69891_16_ITEM2_P0_S0	Our principal properties include twelve production facilities located in ten states, which aggregate approximately two million square feet.
69891_16_ITEM2_P0_S1	We own ten production facilities in the following states: California (2), Georgia, Kansas, Michigan (2), Ohio, Texas, Utah and Washington.
69891_16_ITEM2_P0_S2	Two production facilities, located in Maryland and Florida, are leased subject to agreements that expire through 2020.
69891_16_ITEM2_P0_S3	We believe our facilities are generally in good condition and sufficient to meet our present needs.
69891_16_ITEM2_P1_S0	The production of beverages is capital intensive but is not characterized by rapid technological change.
69891_16_ITEM2_P1_S1	The technological advances that have occurred have generally been of an incremental cost-saving nature, such as the industry s conversion to lighter weight containers or improved blending processes that enhance ingredient yields.
69891_16_ITEM2_P1_S2	We are not aware of any anticipated industry-wide changes in technology that would adversely impact our current physical production capacity or cost of production.
69891_16_ITEM2_P2_S0	We own and lease trucks, vans and automobiles used in the sale, delivery and distribution of our products.
69891_16_ITEM2_P2_S1	In addition, we lease office and warehouse space, transportation equipment, office equipment and certain manufacturing equipment.

69891_16_ITEM3_P0_S1	We do not expect the ultimate disposition of such matters to have a material adverse effect on our consolidated financial position or results of operations.

69891_16_ITEM7_P0_S0	National Beverage Corp. proudly refreshes America with a distinctive portfolio of Sparkling Waters, Juices, Energy Drinks and Carbonated Soft Drinks.
69891_16_ITEM7_P0_S1	We believe that our ingenious product designs, innovative packaging and imaginative flavors, along with our corporate culture and philosophy, makes National Beverage unique in the beverage industry.
69891_16_ITEM7_P1_S0	The Company s primary market focus is the United States, but our products are also distributed in various other countries.
69891_16_ITEM7_P2_S0	National Beverage Corp. was incorporated in Delaware in 1985 and began trading as a public company on the NASDAQ Stock Market in 1991.
69891_16_ITEM7_P2_S1	In this report, the terms we, us, our, Company and National Beverage mean National Beverage Corp. and its subsidiaries unless indicated otherwise.
69891_16_ITEM7_P3_S0	National Beverage is in an ongoing transition to meet the healthy hydration demands of the American consumer.
69891_16_ITEM7_P3_S1	Health and wellness awareness has increased significantly, resulting in growing demand for beverages with little or no calories and wholesome natural ingredients.
69891_16_ITEM7_P4_S0	Our brands emphasize distinctly-flavored beverages in attractive packaging that appeal to multiple demographic groups.
69891_16_ITEM7_P4_S1	The attentive, conscious and discriminating consumer is ever more alert to healthy choices and better-for-you ingredients that align to this transition and strategic focus.
69891_16_ITEM7_P5_S0	Our brands consist of (i) beverages geared to the active and health-conscious consumer ( Power+ Brands ) including sparkling waters, energy drinks, and juices, and (ii) Carbonated Soft Drinks in a variety of flavors including regular, sugar-free and reduced calorie options.
69891_16_ITEM7_P5_S1	To a lesser extent, we produce carbonated soft drinks for specific retailers ( Allied Brands ) that endorse a strategic alliance concept of joint marketing to support growth of both brands.
69891_16_ITEM7_P5_S2	Our portfolio of Power+ Brands includes LaCroix , LaCroix C rate , LaCroix NiCola and Shasta sparkling water products; Rip It energy drinks and shots; and Everfresh , Everfresh Premier Varietals and Mr. Pure 100% juice and juice-based products.
69891_16_ITEM7_P5_S3	Our Carbonated Soft Drinks portfolio includes Shasta and Faygo , iconic brands whose flavor development spans more than 125 years.
69891_16_ITEM7_P6_S0	To service a diverse customer base that includes numerous national retailers, as well as thousands of smaller up-and-down-the-street accounts, we utilize a hybrid distribution system to deliver our products primarily through the take-home, convenience and food-service channels.
69891_16_ITEM7_P7_S0	Our strategy emphasizes the growth of our products by (i) developing healthier beverages in response to the global shift in consumer buying habits and tailoring the variety and types of beverages in our portfolio to satisfy the preferences of a diverse mix of crossover consumers a growing group desiring a change to better-for-you beverages; (ii) emphasizing flavor development and variety throughout our product lines and brands; (iii) producing and developing products of the highest quality that also appeal to the value expectations of the consumer; (iv) leveraging our efficient production and distribution systems, and our cost-effective social media and regionally focused marketing programs, to profitably deliver products at optimal consumer price-points; and (v) responding faster and more creatively to consumer trends than competitors who are burdened by production and distribution complexity as well as legacy costs.
69891_16_ITEM7_P8_S0	The majority of our sales are seasonal with the highest volume typically realized during the summer and warmer months.
69891_16_ITEM7_P8_S1	As a result, our operating results from one fiscal quarter to the next may not be comparable.
69891_16_ITEM7_P8_S2	Additionally, our operating results are affected by numerous factors, including fluctuations in the costs of raw materials, changes in consumer preference for beverage products, competitive pricing in the marketplace and weather conditions.
69891_16_ITEM7_P9_S0	Net Sales Net sales for the fiscal year ended April 30, 2016 ( Fiscal 2016 ) increased 9.1% to $704.8 million compared to $645.8 million for the fiscal year ended May 2, 2015 ( Fiscal 2015 ).
69891_16_ITEM7_P9_S1	The higher sales resulted from a 9.0% increase in case volume and a slight increase in average selling price.
69891_16_ITEM7_P9_S2	The volume increase includes 31.4% growth of our Power+ Brands, partially offset by a decline in branded carbonated soft drinks and Allied Brands.
69891_16_ITEM7_P10_S0	Net sales for Fiscal 2015 increased .7% to $645.8 million compared to $641.1 million for the fiscal year ended May 3, 2014 ( Fiscal 2014 ).
69891_16_ITEM7_P10_S1	The higher sales resulted from a 1.1% increase in case volume partially offset by a .4% decline in average selling price.
69891_16_ITEM7_P10_S2	The increase in case volume reflects a 2.9% increase in branded volume, including a 15.3% case volume growth for our Power+ Brands, partially offset by a decline in Allied Brands.
69891_16_ITEM7_P11_S0	The decline in average selling price is related to changes in product mix.
69891_16_ITEM7_P12_S0	Gross Profit Gross profit for Fiscal 2016 increased 10.2% to $241.4 million compared to $219.1 million for Fiscal 2015.
69891_16_ITEM7_P12_S1	The increase in gross profit is primarily due to higher sales and a decline in cost of sales per case of .4%.
69891_16_ITEM7_P12_S2	The decrease in cost of sales per case was due to favorable product mix changes and lower raw material costs.
69891_16_ITEM7_P12_S3	As a result, gross margin improved to 34.3%.
69891_16_ITEM7_P13_S0	Gross profit was 33.9% of net sales for Fiscal 2015 and Fiscal 2014.
69891_16_ITEM7_P13_S1	Cost of sales per unit declined .3% primarily due to product mix changes.
69891_16_ITEM7_P14_S0	Shipping and handling costs are included in selling, general and administrative expenses, the classification of which is consistent with many beverage companies.
69891_16_ITEM7_P14_S1	However, our gross margin may not be comparable to companies that include shipping and handling costs in cost of sales.
69891_16_ITEM7_P14_S2	See Note 1 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements.
69891_16_ITEM7_P15_S0	Selling, General and Administrative Expenses Selling, general and administrative expenses were $148.4 million or 21.1% of net sales for Fiscal 2016 compared to $145.2 million or 22.5% of net sales for Fiscal 2015.
69891_16_ITEM7_P15_S1	Fiscal 2016 expenses reflect higher distribution, selling and other volume related costs, partially offset by lower marketing costs.
69891_16_ITEM7_P16_S0	Selling, general and administrative expenses were $145.2 million or 22.5% of net sales for Fiscal 2015 compared to $153.2 million or 23.9% of net sales for Fiscal 2014.
69891_16_ITEM7_P16_S1	Fiscal 2015 expenses reflect lower selling and marketing costs.
69891_16_ITEM7_P17_S0	Interest Expense and Other Expense (Income) - Net Interest expense is comprised of interest on borrowings and fees related to maintaining lines of credit.
69891_16_ITEM7_P17_S1	Due to repayments on borrowings, interest expense decreased to $203,000 in Fiscal 2016 from $371,000 in Fiscal 2015 and $660,000 in Fiscal 2014.
69891_16_ITEM7_P17_S2	Other expense is net of interest income of $107,000 for Fiscal 2016, $30,000 for Fiscal 2015 and $15,000 for Fiscal 2014.
69891_16_ITEM7_P17_S3	The change in interest income is due to changes in average invested balances.
69891_16_ITEM7_P17_S4	Other income for Fiscal 2015 includes a $1.3 million gain on sale of property.

69891_16_ITEM7_P26_S0	Financial Position During Fiscal 2016, our working capital increased to $148.1 million from $101.5 million at May 2, 2015.
69891_16_ITEM7_P26_S1	The increase in working capital resulted from higher cash, trade receivables and inventory, partially offset by higher accounts payable and accrued liabilities.
69891_16_ITEM7_P26_S2	Trade receivables increased $1.1 million due to higher sales activity while days sales outstanding improved to 31.0 days from 33.1 days.
69891_16_ITEM7_P26_S3	Inventories increased $5.0 million as a result of the Company maintaining higher finished goods levels to support increases in sales and new product introductions.
69891_16_ITEM7_P26_S4	Annual inventory turns decreased to 9.5 from 10.2 times.
69891_16_ITEM7_P26_S5	At April 30, 2016, the current ratio was 3.0 to 1 compared to 2.5 to 1 at May 2, 2015.
69891_16_ITEM7_P27_S0	During Fiscal 2015, our working capital increased $22.9 million to $101.5 million primarily due to cash generated from operating activities.
69891_16_ITEM7_P27_S1	Trade receivables increased $1.7 million due to higher sales activity and days sales outstanding improved to 33.1 days from 34.7 days.
69891_16_ITEM7_P27_S2	Inventories decreased $1.0 million and annual inventory turns improved to 10.2 from 9.4 times.
69891_16_ITEM7_P27_S3	At May 2, 2015, the current ratio was 2.5 to 1 compared to 2.2 to 1 at May 3, 2014.

69891_16_ITEM7_P35_S0	Credit Risk We sell products to a variety of customers and extend credit based on an evaluation of each customer s financial condition, generally without requiring collateral.
69891_16_ITEM7_P35_S1	Exposure to credit losses varies by customer principally due to the financial condition of each customer.
69891_16_ITEM7_P35_S2	We monitor our exposure to credit losses and maintain allowances for anticipated losses based on specific customer circumstances, credit conditions and historical write-offs.
69891_16_ITEM7_P36_S0	Impairment of Long-Lived Assets All long-lived assets, excluding goodwill and intangible assets not subject to amortization, are evaluated for impairment on the basis of undiscounted cash flows whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable.
69891_16_ITEM7_P36_S1	An impaired asset is written down to its estimated fair market value based on the best information available.
69891_16_ITEM7_P37_S0	Estimated fair market value is generally measured by discounting future cash flows.
69891_16_ITEM7_P38_S0	Goodwill and intangible assets not subject to amortization are evaluated for impairment annually or sooner if we believe such assets may be impaired.
69891_16_ITEM7_P38_S1	An impairment loss is recognized if the carrying amount or, for goodwill, the carrying amount of its reporting unit, is greater than its fair value.
69891_16_ITEM7_P39_S0	Income Taxes Our effective income tax rate is based on estimates of taxes which will ultimately be payable.
69891_16_ITEM7_P39_S1	Deferred taxes are recorded to give recognition to temporary differences between the tax bases of assets or liabilities and their reported amounts in the financial statements.
69891_16_ITEM7_P39_S2	Valuation allowances are established to reduce the carrying amounts of deferred tax assets when it is deemed, more likely than not, that the benefit of deferred tax assets will not be realized.
69891_16_ITEM7_P40_S0	Insurance Programs We maintain self-insured and deductible programs for certain liability, medical and workers compensation exposures.
69891_16_ITEM7_P40_S1	Accordingly, we accrue for known claims and estimated incurred but not reported claims not otherwise covered by insurance based on actuarial assumptions and historical claims experience.
69891_16_ITEM7_P41_S0	We offer various sales incentive arrangements to our customers that require customer performance or achievement of certain sales volume targets.
69891_16_ITEM7_P41_S1	When the incentive is paid in advance, we amortize the amount paid over the period of benefit or contractual sales volume; otherwise, we accrue the expected amount to be paid over the period of benefit or expected sales volume.
69891_16_ITEM7_P41_S2	The recognition of these incentives involves the use of judgment related to performance and sales volume estimates that are made based on historical experience and other factors.
69891_16_ITEM7_P41_S3	Sales incentives are accounted for as a reduction of sales and actual amounts ultimately realized may vary from accrued amounts.

69891_16_ITEM7A_P0_S0	Commodities We purchase various raw materials, including aluminum cans, plastic bottles, high fructose corn syrup, corrugated packaging and juice concentrates, the prices of which fluctuate based on commodity market conditions.
69891_16_ITEM7A_P0_S1	Our ability to recover increased costs through higher pricing may be limited by the competitive environment in which we operate.
69891_16_ITEM7A_P0_S2	At times, we manage our exposure to this risk through the use of supplier pricing agreements that enable us to establish all, or a portion of, the purchase prices for certain raw materials.
69891_16_ITEM7A_P0_S3	Additionally, we use derivative financial instruments to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in certain raw material costs.

69891_16_ITEM7A_P2_S1	If the interest rate on our debt changed by 100 basis points (1%), our interest expense for Fiscal 2016 would have changed by approximately $50,000.

69891_16_ITEM8_P6_S0	Incorporated in Delaware in 1985, National Beverage Corp. is a holding company for various operating subsidiaries.
69891_16_ITEM8_P6_S1	When used in this report, the terms we, us, our, Company and National Beverage mean National Beverage Corp. and its subsidiaries.

69891_16_ITEM8_P7_S1	The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of National Beverage Corp. and all subsidiaries.
69891_16_ITEM8_P7_S2	All significant intercompany transactions and accounts have been eliminated.

69891_16_ITEM8_P8_S0	Cash and Equivalents Cash and equivalents are comprised of cash and highly liquid securities (consisting primarily of short-term money-market investments) with an original maturity of three months or less.
69891_16_ITEM8_P9_S0	Derivative Financial Instruments We use derivative financial instruments to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in raw material costs.
69891_16_ITEM8_P9_S1	All derivative financial instruments are recorded at fair value in our Consolidated Balance Sheets.
69891_16_ITEM8_P9_S2	We do not use derivative financial instruments for trading or speculative purposes.
69891_16_ITEM8_P9_S3	Credit risk related to derivative financial instruments is managed by requiring high credit standards for counterparties and frequent cash settlements.
69891_16_ITEM8_P10_S0	Basic earnings per common share is computed by dividing earnings available to common shareholders by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during the period.
69891_16_ITEM8_P10_S1	Diluted earnings per common share is calculated in a similar manner, but includes the dilutive effect of stock options amounting to 219,000 shares in Fiscal 2016, 206,000 shares in Fiscal 2015 and 188,000 shares in Fiscal 2014.
69891_16_ITEM8_P11_S0	The fair value of long-term debt approximates its carrying value due to its variable interest rate and lack of prepayment penalty.
69891_16_ITEM8_P12_S0	The estimated fair values of derivative financial instruments are calculated based on market rates to settle the instruments.
69891_16_ITEM8_P12_S1	These values represent the estimated amounts we would receive upon sale, taking into consideration current market prices and credit worthiness.

69891_16_ITEM8_P21_S0	New Accounting Pronouncements In March 2016, the Financial Accounting Standards Board ( FASB ) issued Accounting Standards Update 2016-09, Compensation-Stock Compensation: Improvements to Employee Share-Based Payment Accounting ( ASU 2016-9 ).
69891_16_ITEM8_P21_S1	This amendment addresses several aspects of the accounting for share-based payment transactions, including the income tax consequences, classification of awards as either equity or liabilities and classification on the statement of cash flows.
69891_16_ITEM8_P21_S2	ASU 2016-09 is effective for our fiscal year beginning April 30, 2017.
69891_16_ITEM8_P21_S3	We are currently evaluating the potential impact of adopting this guidance on our consolidated financial statements.

69891_16_ITEM8_P22_S1	ASU 2016-02 requires the lease rights and obligations arising from lease contracts, including existing and new arrangements, to be recognized as assets and liabilities on the balance sheet.
69891_16_ITEM8_P22_S2	ASU 2016-02 is effective for our fiscal year beginning April 28, 2019.
69891_16_ITEM8_P22_S3	We are currently evaluating the potential impact of adopting this guidance on our consolidated financial statements.

69891_16_ITEM8_P24_S1	ASU 2014-09 requires an entity to recognize revenue in an amount that reflects the consideration it expects to receive in exchange for goods or services.

69891_16_ITEM8_P25_S0	Property, Plant and Equipment Property, plant and equipment are recorded at cost.
69891_16_ITEM8_P25_S1	Additions, replacements and betterments are capitalized, while maintenance and repairs that do not extend the useful life of an asset are expensed as incurred.
69891_16_ITEM8_P25_S2	Depreciation is recorded using the straight-line method over estimated useful lives of 7 to 30 years for buildings and improvements and 3 to 15 years for machinery and equipment.
69891_16_ITEM8_P25_S3	Leasehold improvements are amortized using the straight-line method over the shorter of the remaining lease term or the estimated useful life of the improvement.
69891_16_ITEM8_P26_S0	When assets are retired or otherwise disposed, the cost and accumulated depreciation are removed from the respective accounts and any related gain or loss is recognized.
69891_16_ITEM8_P27_S0	Revenue Recognition Revenue from product sales is recognized when title and risk of loss pass to the customer, which generally occurs upon delivery.
69891_16_ITEM8_P28_S0	Our policy is not to allow the return of products once they have been accepted by the customer.
69891_16_ITEM8_P28_S1	However, on occasion, we have accepted returns or issued credit to customers, primarily for damaged goods.
69891_16_ITEM8_P28_S2	The amounts have been immaterial and, accordingly, we do not provide a specific valuation allowance for sales returns.
69891_16_ITEM8_P29_S0	We offer various sales incentive arrangements to our customers that require customer performance or achievement of certain sales volume targets.
69891_16_ITEM8_P29_S1	When the incentive is paid in advance, we amortize the amount paid over the period of benefit or contractual sales volume; otherwise, we accrue the expected amount to be paid over the period of benefit or expected sales volume.
69891_16_ITEM8_P29_S2	The recognition of these incentives involves the use of judgment related to performance and sales volume estimates that are made based on historical experience and other factors.
69891_16_ITEM8_P29_S3	Sales incentives are accounted for as a reduction of sales and actual amounts ultimately realized may vary from accrued amounts.
69891_16_ITEM8_P30_S0	We operate as a single operating segment for purposes of presenting financial information and evaluating performance.
69891_16_ITEM8_P30_S1	As such, the accompanying consolidated financial statements present financial information in a format that is consistent with the internal financial information used by management.
69891_16_ITEM8_P30_S2	We do not accumulate revenues by product classification and, therefore, it is impractical to present such information.

69891_16_ITEM8_P50_S0	The Company is a party to a management agreement with Corporate Management Advisors, Inc. ( CMA ), a corporation owned by our Chairman and Chief Executive Officer.
69891_16_ITEM8_P50_S1	This agreement was originated in 1991 for the efficient use of management of two public companies at the time.
69891_16_ITEM8_P50_S2	In 1994, one of those public entities, through a merger, no longer was managed in this manner.
69891_16_ITEM8_P51_S0	Under the terms of the agreement, CMA provides, subject to the direction and supervision of the Board of Directors of the Company, (i) senior corporate functions (including supervision of the Company s financial, legal, executive recruitment, internal audit and management information systems departments) as well as the services of a Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, and (ii) services in connection with acquisitions, dispositions and financings by the Company, including identifying and profiling acquisition candidates, negotiating and structuring potential transactions and arranging financing for any such transaction.
69891_16_ITEM8_P51_S1	CMA, through its personnel, also provides, to the extent possible, the stimulus and creativity to develop an innovative and dynamic persona for the Company, its products and corporate image.
69891_16_ITEM8_P52_S0	In order to fulfill its obligations under the management agreement, CMA employs numerous individuals, whom, acting as a unit, provide management, administrative and creative functions for the Company.
69891_16_ITEM8_P52_S1	The management agreement provides that the Company will pay CMA an annual base fee equal to one percent of the consolidated net sales of the Company, and further provides that the Compensation and Stock Option Committee and the Board of Directors may from time to time award additional incentive compensation to CMA.
69891_16_ITEM8_P52_S2	The Board of Directors on numerous occasions contemplated incentive compensation and, while shareholder value has increased over $2.5 billion (or 6,000%) since the inception of this agreement, no incentive compensation has been paid.
69891_16_ITEM8_P53_S0	We incurred management fees to CMA of $7.0 million for Fiscal 2016, $6.5 million for Fiscal 2015 and $6.4 million for Fiscal 2014.
69891_16_ITEM8_P53_S1	Included in accounts payable were amounts due CMA of $1.8 million at April 30, 2016 and $1.6 million at May 2, 2015.
69891_16_ITEM8_P54_S0	From time to time, we enter into aluminum swap contracts to partially mitigate our exposure to changes in the cost of aluminum cans.
69891_16_ITEM8_P54_S1	Such financial instruments are designated and accounted for as a cash flow hedge.
69891_16_ITEM8_P54_S2	Accordingly, gains or losses attributable to the effective portion of the cash flow hedge are reported in Accumulated Other Comprehensive Income (Loss) ( AOCI ) and reclassified into earnings through cost of sales in the period in which the hedged transaction affects earnings.
69891_16_ITEM8_P55_S0	The ineffective portion of the change in fair value of our cash flow hedge was immaterial.
69891_16_ITEM8_P56_S0	The following summarizes the gains (losses) recognized in the Consolidated Statements of Income and AOCI relative to the cash flow hedge for Fiscal 2016, Fiscal 2015 and Fiscal 2014:

69891_16_ITEM8_P70_S0	Our stock-based compensation program is a broad-based program designed to attract and retain employees while also aligning employees interests with the interests of the shareholders.
69891_16_ITEM8_P71_S0	The 1991 Omnibus Incentive Plan (the Omnibus Plan ) provides for compensatory awards consisting of (i) stock options or stock awards for up to 4,800,000 shares of common stock, (ii) stock appreciation rights, dividend equivalents, other stock-based awards in amounts up to 4,800,000 shares of common stock and (iii) performance awards consisting of any combination of the above.
69891_16_ITEM8_P71_S1	The Omnibus Plan is designed to provide an incentive to officers and certain other key employees and consultants by making available to them an opportunity to acquire a proprietary interest or to increase such interest in National Beverage.
69891_16_ITEM8_P72_S0	The number of shares or options which may be issued under stock-based awards to an individual is limited to 1,680,000 during any year.
69891_16_ITEM8_P72_S1	Awards may be granted for no cash consideration or such minimal cash consideration as may be required by law.
69891_16_ITEM8_P73_S0	Options generally have an exercise price equal to the fair market value of our common stock on the date of grant, vest over a five-year period and expire after ten years.
69891_16_ITEM8_P74_S0	The Special Stock Option Plan provides for the issuance of stock options to purchase up to an aggregate of 1,800,000 shares of common stock.
69891_16_ITEM8_P74_S1	Options may be granted for such consideration as determined by the Board of Directors.
69891_16_ITEM8_P74_S2	The vesting schedule and exercise price of these options are tied to the recipient s ownership level of common stock and the terms generally allow for the reduction in exercise price upon each vesting period.
69891_16_ITEM8_P74_S3	Also, the Board of Directors authorized the issuance of options to purchase up to 50,000 shares of common stock to be issued at the direction of the Chairman.
69891_16_ITEM8_P75_S0	The Key Employee Equity Partnership Program ( KEEP Program ) provides for the granting of stock options to purchase up to 240,000 shares of common stock to key employees, consultants, directors and officers.
69891_16_ITEM8_P75_S1	Participants who purchase shares of stock in the open market receive grants of stock options equal to 50% of the number of shares purchased, up to a maximum of 6,000 shares in any two-year period.
69891_16_ITEM8_P75_S2	Options under the KEEP Program are forfeited in the event of the sale of shares used to acquire such options.
69891_16_ITEM8_P75_S3	Options are granted at an initial exercise price of 60% of the purchase price paid for the shares acquired and the exercise price reduces to the stock par value at the end of the six-year vesting period.
69891_16_ITEM8_P76_S0	We account for stock options under the fair value method of accounting using a Black-Scholes valuation model to estimate the stock option fair value at date of grant.
69891_16_ITEM8_P76_S1	The fair value of stock options is amortized to expense over the vesting period.
69891_16_ITEM8_P76_S2	Stock options granted were 3,500 shares in Fiscal 2016, 276,800 shares in Fiscal 2015 and 5,245 shares in Fiscal 2014.
69891_16_ITEM8_P76_S3	The weighted average Black-Scholes fair value assumptions for stock options granted are as follows: weighted average expected life of 8.0 years for Fiscal 2016, 7.4 years for Fiscal 2015 and 8 years for Fiscal 2014; weighted average expected volatility of 29.0% for Fiscal 2016, 32.8% for Fiscal 2015 and 35.8% for Fiscal 2014; weighted average risk free interest rates of 2.1% for Fiscal 2016, 2.2% for Fiscal 2015 and 1.9% for Fiscal 2014; and expected dividend yield of 3.3% for Fiscal 2016, 4.6% for Fiscal 2015 and 4.6% for Fiscal 2014.
69891_16_ITEM8_P77_S0	The expected life of stock options was estimated based on historical experience.
69891_16_ITEM8_P77_S1	The expected volatility was estimated based on historical stock prices for a period consistent with the expected life of stock options.
69891_16_ITEM8_P77_S2	The risk free interest rate was based on the U.S. Treasury constant maturity interest rate whose term is consistent with the expected life of stock options.
69891_16_ITEM8_P77_S3	Forfeitures were estimated based on historical experience and ranged from 0% to 16% for Fiscal 2016, Fiscal 2015 and Fiscal 2014.

69891_16_ITEM8_P97_S0	We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of National Beverage Corp. as of April 30, 2016 and May 2, 2015 and the related consolidated statements of income, comprehensive income, shareholders equity and cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended April 30, 2016.
69891_16_ITEM8_P97_S1	We also have audited National Beverage Corp. s internal control over financial reporting as of April 30, 2016, based on criteria established in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO) in 2013.
69891_16_ITEM8_P97_S2	National Beverage Corp. s management is responsible for these financial statements, for maintaining effective internal control over financial reporting and for its assessment of the effectiveness of internal control over financial reporting included in the accompanying Management s Report on Internal Control over Financial Reporting.
69891_16_ITEM8_P97_S3	Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements and an opinion on the Company s internal control over financial reporting based on our audits.
69891_16_ITEM8_P98_S0	We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).
69891_16_ITEM8_P98_S1	Those standards require that we plan and perform the audits to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement and whether effective internal control over financial reporting was maintained in all material respects.
69891_16_ITEM8_P98_S2	Our audits of the financial statements included examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management and evaluating the overall financial statement presentation.
69891_16_ITEM8_P98_S3	Our audit of internal control over financial reporting included obtaining an understanding of internal control over financial reporting, assessing the risk that a material weakness exists and testing and evaluating the design and operating effectiveness of internal control based on the assessed risk.
69891_16_ITEM8_P98_S4	Our audits also included performing such other procedures as we considered necessary in the circumstances.
69891_16_ITEM8_P98_S5	We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinions.
69891_16_ITEM8_P99_S0	A company s internal control over financial reporting is a process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
69891_16_ITEM8_P99_S1	A company s internal control over financial reporting includes those policies and procedures that (1) pertain to the maintenance of records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect the transactions and dispositions of the assets of the company; (2) provide reasonable assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary to permit preparation of financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles and that receipts and expenditures of the company are being made only in accordance with authorizations of management and directors of the company; and (3) provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition, use, or disposition of the company s assets that could have a material effect on the financial statements.
69891_16_ITEM8_P100_S0	Because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
69891_16_ITEM8_P100_S1	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or that the degree of compliance with the policies or procedures may deteriorate.
69891_16_ITEM8_P101_S0	In our opinion, the consolidated financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of National Beverage Corp. as of April 30, 2016 and May 2, 2015 and the results of their operations and their cash flows for each of the years in the three-year period ended April 30, 2016, in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.
69891_16_ITEM8_P101_S1	Also in our opinion, National Beverage Corp. maintained, in all material respects, effective internal control over financial reporting as of April 30, 2016, based on criteria established in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO) in 2013.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P0_S0	Disclosure Controls and Procedures As of the end of the period covered by this Annual Report on Form 10-K, we carried out an evaluation, under the supervision and with the participation of the Company s management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, of the effectiveness of the design and operation of our disclosure controls and procedures (as defined in Rule 13a-15(e) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the Exchange Act )).
69891_16_ITEM9A_P0_S1	Based upon that evaluation, the Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer concluded that our disclosure controls and procedures were effective to ensure information required to be disclosed by us in reports we file or submit under the Exchange Act is (1) recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified in SEC rules and forms and (2) accumulated and communicated to our management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, to allow timely decisions regarding required disclosure.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P1_S0	Our management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting, as such term is defined in Rule 13a-15(f) of the Exchange Act.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P1_S1	Under the supervision and with the participation of our management, including our Chief Executive Officer and Principal Financial Officer, we conducted an evaluation of the effectiveness of our internal control over financial reporting based on the framework in Internal Control Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission in 2013.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P1_S2	Based on that evaluation, our management concluded that our internal control over financial reporting was effective as of April 30, 2016.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Management recognizes that there are inherent limitations in the effectiveness of any internal control over financial reporting, including the possibility of human error and the circumvention or overriding of internal control.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P2_S1	Accordingly, even effective internal control over financial reporting can provide only reasonable assurance with respect to financial statement preparation.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P2_S2	Further, because of changes in conditions, the effectiveness of internal control may vary over time.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P3_S0	RSM US LLP, an independent registered public accounting firm, has audited the consolidated financial statements included in this Annual Report on Form 10-K and, as part of their audit, has issued their report, included herein, on the effectiveness of our internal control over financial reporting.
69891_16_ITEM9A_P4_S0	Changes in Internal Control over Financial Reporting There were no changes in our internal control over financial reporting during the quarter ended April 30, 2016 that have materially affected, or are reasonably likely to materially affect, our internal control over financial reporting.

69891_17_ITEM1_P0_S0	The information required by Item 13 will be included under the captions Certain Relationships and Related Party Transactions and Information Regarding Meetings and Committees of the Board in the Company s 2017 Proxy Statement and is incorporated herein by reference.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P0_S0	In addition to other information in this Annual Report on Form 10-K, the following risk factors should be considered carefully in evaluating the Company s business.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P0_S1	Our business, financial condition and results of operations could be materially and adversely affected by any of these risks.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P0_S2	Additional risks and uncertainties, including risks and uncertainties not presently known to the Company, or that the Company currently deems immaterial, may also impair our business and results of operations.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P1_S0	Our beverage portfolio is comprised of a number of unique brands with reputations and consumer imagery that have been built over time.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P1_S1	Our investments in social media and marketing as well as our strong commitment to product quality are intended to have a favorable impact on brand image and consumer preferences.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P1_S2	Unfavorable publicity, or allegations of quality issues, even if false or unfounded, could tarnish our reputation and brand image and may cause consumers to choose other products.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P1_S3	In addition, if we do not adequately anticipate and react to changing demographics, consumer trends, health concerns and product preferences, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P2_S0	The beverage industry is extremely competitive.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P2_S1	Our products compete with a broad range of beverage products, most of which are manufactured and distributed by companies with substantially greater financial, marketing and distribution resources.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P2_S2	In order to generate future revenues and profits, we must continue to sell products that appeal to our customers and consumers.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P2_S3	Discounting and other actions by our competitors may make it more difficult to sustain revenues and profits.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P3_S0	Our retail customer base has been consolidating over the last several years resulting in fewer customers with increased purchasing power.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P3_S1	This increased purchasing power can limit our ability to increase pricing for our products with certain of our customers.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P3_S2	Additionally, E-commerce transactions and value stores are experiencing rapid growth.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P3_S3	Our inability to adapt to customer requirements could lead to a loss of business and adversely affect our financial results.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P4_S0	The production of our products is dependent on certain raw materials, including aluminum, resin, corn, linerboard, water and fruit juice.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P4_S1	In addition, the production and distribution of our products is dependent on energy sources, including natural gas, fuel and electricity.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P4_S2	These items are subject to price volatility caused by numerous factors.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P4_S3	Commodity price increases ultimately result in a corresponding increase in the cost of raw materials and energy.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P4_S4	We may be limited in our ability to pass these increases on to our customers or may incur a loss in sales volume to the extent price increases are taken.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P4_S5	In addition, strikes, weather conditions, governmental controls, national emergencies, natural disasters, supply shortages or other events could affect our continued supply of raw materials and energy.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P4_S6	If raw materials or energy costs increase, or the availability is limited, our financial results could be adversely affected.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P5_S0	Our business and properties are subject to various federal, state and local laws and regulations, including those governing the production, packaging, quality, labeling and distribution of beverage products.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P5_S1	In addition, various governmental agencies have enacted or are considering additional taxes on soft drinks and other sweetened beverages.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P5_S2	Changes in existing laws or regulations could require material expenses and negatively affect our financial results through lower sales or higher costs.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P6_S0	Sustained increases in the cost of employee benefits.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P6_S1	Our profitability is affected by the cost of medical and retirement benefits provided to employees, including employees covered under collective bargaining agreements and multi-employer pension plans.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P6_S2	In recent years, we have experienced increases in these costs as a result of certain factors beyond our control.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P6_S3	Although we seek to limit these cost increases, continued upward pressure in these costs could reduce our profitability.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P7_S0	Unfavorable weather conditions could have an adverse impact on our revenue and profitability.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P7_S1	Unusually cold or rainy weather may temporarily reduce demand for our products and contribute to lower sales, which could adversely affect our profitability for such periods.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P7_S2	Prolonged drought conditions in the geographic regions in which we do business could lead to restrictions on the use of water, which could adversely affect our ability to produce and distribute products.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P8_S0	Our performance significantly depends upon the continued contributions of our executive officers and key employees, both individually and as a group, and our ability to retain and motivate them.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P8_S1	Our officers and key personnel have many years of experience with us and in our industry and it may be difficult to replace them.
69891_17_ITEM1A_P8_S2	If we lose key personnel or are unable to recruit qualified personnel, our operations and ability to manage our business may be adversely affected.
69891_17_ITEM2_P0_S0	Our principal properties include twelve production facilities located in ten states, which aggregate approximately two million square feet.
69891_17_ITEM2_P0_S1	We own ten production facilities in the following states: California (2), Georgia, Kansas, Michigan (2), Ohio, Texas, Utah and Washington.
69891_17_ITEM2_P0_S2	Two production facilities, located in Maryland and Florida, are leased subject to agreements that expire through 2020.
69891_17_ITEM2_P0_S3	We believe our facilities are generally in good condition and sufficient to meet our present needs.
69891_17_ITEM2_P1_S0	The production of beverages is capital intensive but is not characterized by rapid technological change.
69891_17_ITEM2_P1_S1	The technological advances that have occurred have generally been of an incremental cost-saving nature, such as the industry s conversion to lighter weight containers or improved blending processes that enhance ingredient yields.
69891_17_ITEM2_P1_S2	Although we are continually investing in more efficient equipment, we are not aware of any anticipated industry-wide changes in technology that would adversely impact our current physical production capacity or cost of production.
69891_17_ITEM2_P2_S0	We own and lease trucks, vans and automobiles used in the sale, delivery and distribution of our products.
69891_17_ITEM2_P2_S1	In addition, we lease warehouse and office space, transportation equipment, office equipment and certain manufacturing equipment.
69891_17_ITEM3_P0_S0	From time to time, we are a party to various litigation matters and claims arising in the ordinary course of business.
69891_17_ITEM3_P0_S1	We do not expect the ultimate disposition of such matters to have a material adverse effect on our consolidated financial position or results of operations.
